The ensamples of Virtue and vice, gathered out of holy scripture. By Nicolas
Hanape patriarch of Jerusalem. Uery necessary for all christen men and women
to look upon.

And Englyshed by Thomas Paynell.

Anno. 1561.

To the most noble, most excellent, and most virtuous Lady Elizabeth. Queen
of England, France, and Irelande, defender of the faith. etc. Thomas Paynel
wishes all felicity.
ALthough your gracious life to all men's judgments, is so clean and pure
that it neade no manner of incitatyon or ensample of virtue to virtuous and
charitable living: yet when I bethought me how corrupt, how caduke, how
bryttle, and how sliding from virtue to vice, man's nature is even from the
beginning, and with how diverse and manifold instigations the concupiscences and
lusts of this deceitful world does embrace and entangle man with all, and
that our adversary the devil is most vigilante and diligente daily to devour
the soul of man, and to alure him to his ways and tradityons: ^. Peter. 5.
I esteemed it irreprehensible, if I your daily orator should at any time, I say
not quicken your grace, for tha^ were but lost labor, but exhort your grace to
the continuance of your godly and virtuous living, and judged my sel^
unblameable, if I in this tempes^ious and blustryng time should send your grace,
as it were an anchor, or a staff to stay you by, and fermely to stablyshe your
grace, least that your grace should (that God forbid) waver or slide from the
Catholic and true faith of God, from his true and liuelye word, or from the
trace of your charitable and virtuous living. For who is sure to stand fast,
and not to fall? Paul says. Let him that stands take heed he fall not. Or
who can say, I am without syn, or my heart is clean? What is more surer then
to avoid this fall, than to lean to thinfallible and mighty word of God, than
to ensue the life of Christ our savior and and redeamer, and the ensamples and
undoubted hystories, gathered out of holy scripture, and by me your highness
most hable and obedient subject translated for the vtilitye and consolation of
the unlearned into english: this is doubtless a very profitable colection,
and the anchor and staff that I spoke of, containing most compendiously the
wonderful miracles, the noble historyes, the worthy acts, the wise sayings,
the politic stratagemes the wicked co^spiracies, the due obedience, faith and
fidelitye of a christian, with other innumerable and marvelous things, and ye
parables of all scripture. Read it therefore most gracious Lady, and take good
hold at the godly ensamples and doctrines there of, for in so doing, your
grace shall not neade to slide from the faith of Christ, nor yet from the
trace of your godly and virtuous life, but shall stand as Christ's soldier
against satan, the world, and the flesh to your eternal felicity and comfort
most victoriously. For where there is no pain nor battle, there can be no
victory nor no triumph. For Sayncte Paul says, Act. 14.
that we through much tribulation and pain, must enter into the kingdom of
God. And again he says, 2. Cor. 4
that this our tribulation and adversity which is momentanye and light,
prepares an exceadynge and an eternal weight of glory unto us: yea and that a
crown of righteousness is laid up for all those that suffer tribulation and
adversity, 1. Timo. 4.
and have fought a good fight, and have kept their faith, the which our Lord
that is a righteous judge shall give unto all them that love his coming. And
for as much as this our slidinge life, is as it were but a warfare and a
continual battle against our ghostly enemi the devil, fight ye must yea and
that earnestly and continually even to the latter end, for so your grace shall
ouerturne satan your enemy most victoriouslye, and be crowned with the
crown of eternal joy and felicity.

An exhortation to the study of holy scripture.
THou shall show thy son in that day, saying. Deute. 12.
This is that which our Lord did unto me, when I came out of Egypt. And it
shall be as a sign unto thee upon thine hand, and for a remembrance before
thine eyes, that our Lords law may be always in thy mouth. For in a strong
hand our lord brought thee out of Egypt.

Ye shall not do that, that seems good in your own eyes, Deute. 13.
but that I command you, that do you only unto our lord, nor thou shall put
naught thereto, nor take ought there from.

Thou shall read thys^ law before al Israel in their ears. Deute. 31
Gather the people together, men, women, and children, and the stranger that is
within thy gates, that they may hear and learn, and fear our Lord your God.
And keep and observe all the words of this law.

Let not the book of this law depart out of thy mouth, but record therein day
and night, that thou may observe and do according to all that is written
therein, for then thou shall make thy way prosperous, and then shalt thou do
wiselye. Iosu. 1.
Thou shall not decline from the words of this law neither to the right hand,
nor to the left, that thou may do al thing wiselye that thou take in hand.

All the words of God are pure and clean, for he is a shield unto all them,
Prouer. 30.
that put their trust in him. Put thou nothing unto his words, least he
reprove thee, and thou be found a lier.

Cry now as loud as thou canste, leave not of, lift up thy voice like a
trompet, and show my people their offenses, Esaias. 58
and the house of Jacob their sins.

Woe be unto those folish prophets that follow their own spirit, Ezech. 13
and speak where they se nothing.

Search the scriptures, John. 5.
for they are they, which testifye of me.

What so ever things are written, 1. Mat. 15.
they are written for our learning, that we through pacyente and comfort of
the scriptures, might have hope.

2. Timo. 4.
Al scripture given by inspiration of God, is profitable to teach, to improve,
to amend, and to instruct in rightwisenes that the man of God may be perfect
and prepared unto al good works.

Of Miracles showed by the divine power of God. The first Chapter.
THe creatyon of things was so marvelous, that the knowledge thereof could
not come to man, but by revelation. For after the mind of S. Gregory, Greg.
super zac. homeli. 1.
Moses prophesied of those things that were past, saying. In the beginning God
created heaven and earth. Genesis. 1.
Nor that, because he forspoke the things that were to come, but because he
disclosed those things that were seacreat.

At the time of Noyes floude, Gene. 6.7.
our Lord saved Noah, his wife, his three sons with their wives: and in the
Arc he saved the male and the female of all other beasts.

Our Lord repressed the presumpteousnesse of men, Gene. 11.
that would build a tower unto heaven: confoundinge their language.

Genesis. 22
Isaac was wonderfully born, and wonderfully delivered, when that he (the ram
being caught by the horns in a thicket) should have been offered up for a
sacrifice.

Exodus 7.8.9. and.10.
It is euidente and plain inoughe how many miracles our Lord showed by Moses,
when he brought the Children of Israel out of Egypt.

Exodus. 13.
It was a great miracle, that the Pyllare of the cloud departed not from the
Children of Israel going out of Egipte toward the land of promise,
neither by day, nor yet by night.

Exodus. 14
It was a terrible, and a Miracle worthy to be spoken of, that the red sea was
divided, and so dried up, that the children of Israel went over dry footed,
and the Egyptyans overwhelmed in the myddest of the sluds.

Exodus. 15
By the wood or tree showed unto Moses, the waters were made sweet.

Numer. 11.
Our Lord sent quails to the murmuring people, Nume. 20.
and afterward it rained Manna for them to eat, and out of the rock, he sent
them water plenteously to drink.

Our Lord sent flesh to the children of Israel, Numer. 20
the which in the wilderness murmured and desired to eat flesh even
aboundauntly.

Through thoccasion of Chore and his fellows sedition, Nu. 16.17.
many miracles chanced and was showed.

The people were smitten or stinged with fiery serpents, Numer. 21.
and loking upon the serpente of brass, they were cured and healed.

Our Lord led the children of Israel in the wilderness fortye year, Deute.
26.
and their clothes waxed not old, nor their shoes were not consumed upon their
fete.

There was a certain man at Listra the which was a crepel from his mothers
womb, Acts. 14.
and never had walked unto whom Paul loking upon him, said with a loud
voice. Stand upright on thy fete, and he start up and walcked.

Nume. xxii
Balaam coming to curse gods people, was reproved of the ass, that he rode
upon.

Iosu. iii.
After that the children of Israel were entered into the flood of Jordan, the
waters that came down from above, did swell and rise up upon an heap like a
mountain, and the waters that were beneath departed into the dead or salt Sea.

Iosue, vi.
After that the children of Israel had compassed the city of Jericho vii.
times, the wall fell down.

Iosu. x.
Our Lord obeyed to Io^ues vow, saying. Sun stand thou still upon Gabeon.

Iosu, vii.
Our Lord sent the sweard into all the hosts of the Medianites, and they slew
one a another: so that by a few, many were ouercommed and discomfited.

iii. Reg. v.
By our Lord's Ark, the which the Philistines took, were many miracles showed.

i. Reg. xiiii
Ionathas and his Harness bearer destroyed so many of the Philistines, that it
was taken for a miracle, and all the hosts were troubled.

This likewise was no small thing that David, 1. regum. 17
being but young, inexpert and unarmed, prevailed against that strong and
armed Philistiane Goliath.

It is red, 3. regum. 17
that Helias did miracles, as when he asked of God such a drought, that it
rained not upon thearth, for the space of three years and a half.

Likewise the ravens brought him bread and flesh twice every day. 3. regum. 17


Consequentlye he revived the woman's child. 3. regum. 17


Afterward through prayers, 3. regum. ^8
he obtained of God fire, that wonderfully consumed the burnt sacrifice, and
after his Prayer there was a great rain.

After this the angel of our Lord showed him bread and water. 4. regum. 1.
And through his prayers, the fire burnte up ii. captains over fiftye with
their fiftyes.

At length he divided the waters of Jordan with his mantel, 4. regum. 2
and was taken up in a charet of fire into heaven.

4. regu. 4.
Many like things are written of Helizeus, for the increased the poor widows
oil, that was indetted.

4 regu. 4.
The self obtained a child for the sunamite. And after it was departed he
revived it again.

4. regu. 4.
He cast meal into the pottage that was first bitter, and made it sweet. And
multiplied the loves for the prophets children.

4. regum. 5.
He healed Naaman the Sirian of his leprosy.

4. regum. 6
He makes iron to swim upon the water.

4. regum. 6
He knew many things being absent, as though he had been present. And caused
his servant to see the fiery charets of Angels. And he smote the hoastes of
the Assiryans with blindness.

4. reg. 7.8
Uery often he prognosticated things that were to come.

4. regu. 13.
The carkase of a certain dead man touching the body of Elizeus revived.

4. regu. 19.
When king Sennacherib besieged the city of La^his, three were slain of his men
in one night, an hundred, four score and five thousand, in the days and time
of king Ezechiell.

The children of Ammon, 2. Para. 20.
of Moab, and of the mount of Seir, gathered the^ selves together against king
Iosaphat, and what time the Levites began to laud and praise GOD in the host
of Iosaphat, their adversaries tourninge their weapons against them selves,
and murdered one an other.

This thing was very maruailous, 4. reg. 20
that the Sun at the peticyon of Ezechia went ten lines or degrees
backewarde in the Dyall of Achaz.

Tobias was four years blind, Tob. 11.
but afterward by the angels counsel, he anointed his eyes with the gall of
the Fish, and received his sight.

The miracle of Daniels three fellows, Daniel. 3.
and how magnificentlye they were delivered from the furnace of burning fire,
is worthy to be remembered.

Daniell. 6.
Likewise how that Daniel remained vii. days with the Lions vnhurted.

Jonas. 1.2.
By Jonas occasion, the Sea was sore troubled, but after they had cast him into
the Sea, a fish swallowed him up, and he lived there three dais, and
afterward escaped and came out safe and sound.

2. Macha. 3
Heliodorus proved the might and power of God, when he would have spoiled the
temple. For he was beaten and scourged of two young men very grievously.

2. Macha. 8
There pearished against the Galathians in Babylon.6000. men through the aid
of 12000. men sent unto them from heaven.

Luke. 1.
The Angel of our Lord appeared unto Zachary, declaringe unto him from God,
that Helizabeth his baren and old wife should bear him a son, the which
geuinge no credence to the Angels words, was made domme until the child was
circumcised: and then his speech was restored him again.

And this was very marvelous that Ihon, Luke. 1.
being yet in his mothers wo^b reioysed and sprange at the salutation of
blessed Mary, the which had newly conceived our savior. And when blessed
Elizabeth knew it, she reioysed, saying. Blessed art thou among women.

And also that there came wise men from the East to Jerusalem, Mathe. 2.
a star leading and going before them.

Our Lord Jesus being called to the marriage, Ihon. 2.
at the beginnynge of his miracles, turned water into wine.

Nor this was no small miracle of our Lord, Luke. 4.
that he when they of Nazareth filled with wrath led him even to the edge of
the hill, that they might cast him down headlonge, went his way even through
the midst of them.

And Jesus went about, Math. 4.
and they brought unto him all sick people, and he healed them.

As for the miracles which our savior vouchsaued to do being conuersaunt
among the people, are gathered out of the Evangelical historye. For he
revived three dead men, that is the Daughter of Ia^rus the Archsinagoge, Math.
9.
and the widows son that was carried out of the City. Luke. 7.
The third was Lazarus. Ihon. 11.
After that he healed a leven leapers. Of the one Math. viii. Luke. v. Of the
other ten. Luke. xvii.

Afterward he gave six blind men their sight. Of two Math. ix. of other
two. Math. xx. Of one other. Mark. viii. Of him that was borne blind. Ihon. ix.

He deliuerd vii. specially that were possessed of Devils. Of two of them.
Matthew. viii. Of the one of them, the which was most famous, whose name as
he said was called Legio, is touched. Luke. viii. Of one other, the which was
blind and dumme. Math. xii. Of a certain Lunatyke, the which could not be
delivered but by Prayer and Fasting. Math. xvii. Mark. ix. And of an other
unclean spirit that was cast out of a man in the Jews Synnagoge. Mark.
i. Luke. iiii. and of the woman of Cananes daughter, that was healed at the
instaunce and prayer of her mother. Math. xv.

Furthermore it is showed after the sense of the letter. Luke viii. that he
cast out seven devils out of Marye. Mark. xvii.

When that Simo^s mother in law was taken and vexed with a great Fever, Luke.
4.
he rebuked the Fever, and immediatlye she arose and ministered unto them. Math.
viii. Mar. i.

He healed a man (which was let down through the tilinge) of the Palsy.
Lu. 5.


Also as he was eating in the Pharisees house on the Sabbath day, Luke 14
he healed him that had the dropsy.

And he erected and made straighte the woman that bowed together, Lu. 13
and could in no wise look vpwardes, nor lift up her head.

He caused the man that had a wythered hand, mar. 3.
to stretche forth his hand.

Math. 8.
He healed also the Captains servant, that lay sick of the palsy.

Mar. 7.
Item he made the dumme to speak and the deaf to hear.

Ihon. 4.
He heals the rulers son of Capernaum that was even at the point of death.

Mar. 15.
He caused by the only touching of the hemme of his garmente, the issue of
blood to cease and to be stopped in the woman.

Mar. 4.
Our Lord being a sleep, there arose a great tempest or storm in the s^a, he
rebuked the winds, and eftsoon the wind and the Sea obeyed him.

math. 14.
He walked on the sea, his disciples wondering there at, and he made Peter to
walcke on the water, and stretching forth his hand, he saved Peter that began
to sink.

Mar. 9.
He showed a fair miracle to those three Discyples in his Transfyguration.

mar. 6.
He satisfied with v. loves and two fishes, five thousand men, and they took up
xii. baskets.

At another time and season he refreshed with seven loves and a few little
fishes ^oure thousand men, Math. 15
and they took up vii. baskets full.

He cursed the Fig tree having leaves only without fruit, Math. 21
and inco^tinently it withered away.

Gently he restored the princes servant his ear that Peter smote of, Math.
26.
and checked Peter for the same.

When that our savior was hanging upon the Cross, from the syxte hour to
the ninthe hour, Luke. 23.
there was darkness over all the earth, the none being on the contrary part of
ye sky, so that the Sun could in no wise suffer any Eclipse by that moan.
math. 27.
And the veil of the temple did rent, and the graves did open.

At the resurrection and vprising of our Lord, math. 28.
there was a great earthquake, for the angel of our Lord descended from
heaven, and came and rouled back the stone. etc. and for fear the kepers were
astonished.

After this he appeared to his disciples, Ihon. 20.
the doors being shut.

Ihon. 21.
Afterward did Jesus show him self again at the Sea of Tiberias, where at his
Commandment they cast out their net, and it was fylde with great
Fyshes, a hundred and liii. yet was not the net broken.

And xl. days after his resurrection, appearinge unto his Disciples, and
rebukinge and instructynge them, Acts. 1.
while they beheld and maruailed, he was taken up an hie, and a cloud received
him up out of their sight.

These forsaide miracles are spoken of in special. Many other were done (as
we read) in general. As it appears in diverse places of Mathewe. Ihon. 21.
Mark and Luke. And Ihon says: That there are many other things, which
Jesus did, the which if they should be written, I suppose ye world could not
contain the books that should be written.

Act^s. 2.
It was no small miracle of the effusion of the holy sprite, upon the disciples
at Pentecost, where with the disciples were fortified, made steadfast, and
illuminated.

Peter beholdynge a lame man at the gate of the Temple, Acts. 3
which was called beautiful, said: In the name of Jesus rise up, and walk,
and taking him by the right hand, he lift him up, and his fete and ancle
bones recovered strength.

The chief priest, Acts. 5
and al they that were with him, laid hands on the Apostles, and put them
in the common Prysonne. But the Angel of our Lord by night opened the
prison doors, and brought them forth.

They brought the sick into the streates, Acts. 5
and laid them on Beds and cowches, that at the least way, the shadow of
Peter, when he came by, might shaddowe some of them. There came also a
multitude out of the cities round about, and they were all healed.

When Phillip preached at Samaria, Act. 8.
unclean sprites, crying with loud voices came out of many, and many taken with
Palsies, and many that halted, were healed.

Acts. 9.
Peter healed one Eneas which had kept his bed of the palsy viii. years. He
said unto him, Eneas? our Lord Jesus shall make thee whole.

Acts. 9.
Peter put all other forth, and kneling down, he prayed, and turninge him to
the body, he said: Tabitha, arise, and she opened her eyes, and when she saw
Peter, she sat up.

Acts. 9.
This was a marvelous deed, that as Saul was going to Damasco, to take Christ's
disciples, there shyned round about him a light from heaven, and he fell to
the earth. Inwardly he was illuminated, and outwardly he was blineded.

Acts. 12.
Peter being in prison, bound with two chains, and kept most diligently with
iiii. quaternions of Soldiers, was losed and brought forth by the Angel of
God, and the iron gate opened to the^ by the own accord.

Acts. 13.
Paul did deprive Elimas the sorcerer and false prophet of his syghte, because
he sought to turn Paul the Proconsul and ruler from the faith: and resysted
against the Apostels,

A certain damsel possessed with a spirit that prophesied, brought her
master and mistres much vauntage with prophesying. The same followed Paul and
Luke, Acts. 16.
and cried, saying: These men are the servants of the most hie God. But Paul
said to the spirit, I command thee in the name of Jesus, that thou come out of
her, and he came out the same hour.

Paul and Silas were in prison, and prayed, Acts. 16.
and lauded God. And suddenly there was a great earthquake, so that the
foundation of the prysone was shaken, and immediately all the doors opened, and
every man's bands were losed.

God wrought no small miracles by the hands of Paul: so that from his body
were brought unto the sick, Acts. 19.
napkins and partlettes, and the diseases departed from them, and the euel
sprites went out of them.

Certain Jews took upon them to ^al over them, Acts. 19.
which had euel sprites ^he name of our Lord Jesus, saying: we adjure you by
Jesus whom Paul preaches. And the evil sprite answered and said. Jesus I
know, and Paul I know, but who are ye? and the man in whom the evil sprite
was ran on them, and prevailed against them, so that they fled away naked
and wounded.

And upon one of the sabbath days Paul preached, and continued the preachinge
unto midnight. Acts. 20.
And there satte in a window a certain young manne, being fallen into a dead
sleep. And overcome with sleep, he fell down from the third lofte, and was
taken up dead. But when Paul went down, he fell on him, and embrased him. And
they brought the young man a live, and were not a little comforted.

And in the Winter when Paul and his fellows were escaped out of the broken
ship, Acts. 28.

Our Lord suffered that Antiochus should make that venerable and reverent temple

burn the holy city, and make great slaughter of Innocents.

In the days and time of Antiochus Epiphanius, 1. Macha. 6
the which destroyed the Temple, and made it Profane, did cruelly handle many
of ye Jews, and slew them. It might apeare and seem to many, that the whole
world was in a confusion, and evil ordained and ruled. But for all that our
Lord out of those evils, could bring the punishmente of the wicked, and the
corruption of certain other. And again the virtue and merits of many of
those that were slain, were diversely increased.

I pray those that hear this, to consider, how that Judas Machabeus,
Ionathas, 1. Macha. 9. 1. Match. 10
and Simon his brethren were men toward God and men most valiant and most
faithful: and yet they died but miserably. For Judas was slain in battle

In our Lords passion, God, as concerning the redemption of mankind,
fulfilled his most benign will by the most celerate and wicked iniquity of
men. Acts. 3
For scripture says God which before had showed, by the mouth of all his

Ihon. 18.
Peter the Prince of the Apostles, and head of the Church, denied his master

Ihon. 11.
Thomas, the which said so confedently. Let us go, that we may dye with him,
doubted of our Lords resurrection, whereof it came that Peter was the more
meke and gentle to sinners, and that the faithful, and they that stackard in
the faith, were the better stablished there in. And of this it is gathered,
that no man should presume upon his stedfastnes. And that no man, whether he
be fallen from his faith, or doubts therein should despair of the mercy, or
of the forgiveness of God. And by this that Judas the Apostle and dispensator
of God did slide into such an eanorme crime, nor rose not again, al
presu^pteous security is deminished and broken: by the which no man for the
state and condition that he is in, nor for the deeds that he has done ought
to be hie mineded, but in fear. For why the Apostles were the faithful leaders
of the people, and yet they were kept in prysonne wythal diligence.

It might seem to such as be weak, that God should not have suffered such
things to have been done in the beginning of the faith. Acts. 4^
But yet ye faithful thereby were maruelously comforted, and the adversaries of
our faith confuted. Acts. 12.
The like thing chanced in Peter alone when he was taken by Herod, put in
prison, and brought forth and miraculouslye delivered by the Angel.

It was great iniquity to stone Steven to death, Acts. 7.
and yet many good things through the providence of God, came thereof. For
Steven was gloriously crowned in heaven, and aboundauntly honored in earth,
his oration and prayer that he made there, brought Paul unto us, and left unto
al our posterity an example of a marvelous pa^ience and charity.

Acts. 8
Steven being thus stoned, there followed a great persecution in the Church
and congregation that was at Jerusalem.

For they were all sparkled abroad through out all the regions of Iewry and
Samaria, except the Apostles, so that ^t seemed to be a great detriment or
hindera^ce to ye honor of the christian religion. But the Discyples that were
scattered abroad did so preach and set forth the word of God, that the
Church there by was a great deal the more enlarged.

Acts. 13.
For as much as the Jews, when Paul and Barnabas preached the word of God
unto them, refused it, and put it from them, they took an occasyon to preach
unto the Gentyles.

There was a dissentyon between Paul and Barnabas for Iho^ whose surname was
Mark, whom Paul would not receive, because he went from the^, but Barnabas
took Mark with him, Acts. 15.
and so they departed a sunder one from the other. Where by should have
followed, as it was thought, some great rebuke and shame. But God disposing
the matter, there ensued great fruit and profit. For the word of God was
opened and preached to many.

They committed a very heinous deed and fault, that put that excellent
doctoure Paul in prison, co^pellynge him to cease from Preachinge, the which
thing might seem to many, a great inconvenience, and that God should not have
suffered it.

And yet it is to be greatly noted, that the divine providence by such
impedimentes and losses, has showed and caused great fruit and profit.

For as the merits of Paul did thereby increase, so likewise he left the mo
examples of virtue, and taught much better by his works, then before time
by his words. For being in prison, he wrote to those that were absent and in
far countries, nether was he so profitable unto the church by his preachinge,
as he was by sending of his Epistles. And therefore if he in any one city or
province had been honored of all men, and gladly hardt he should not yet have
had such occasions to have gone and visited so diverse and many nations as he
visited. Therefore when that the Jews, or any other did persecute him from
town to town, he preached the word of God to many. And when he was in
hold, he wrote his Epistles, and when the Jews resisted him, Acts. 13.
he turned him self to the gentiles.

And again, because that in Syria, he found Festus and Felix unrightful
Judges, Acts. 25.
he was enforced to appeal to Caesar, and so he came to Rome, and through
his predication and doctrine was greatly illustred, and luckelye by his passion
made most famous.

Dani. 3.
The Angel of our Lord came down with Azaria and his fellows, into the
Oven, and smote the flame of fire out of the Oven, and made in the midst of
the oven, as it had been a cold wind blowing, so that the fire neither touched
them, grieved them, nor did them hurt. Whereby it appears that the divine
pity is in every place, and ready at all times to comfort man.

Of the anger and fury of God.
NOte and take heed, that ye anger of God, De ciuitate dei. Lib. 15 Capitu. 25.
after ye mind of S. Augustine, is not the perturbation or motyon of his mind,
but his judgment, by the which, pain is appointed to sin, his cogytatyon
and recogytation of things mutable, is his immutable reason and judgment.
Nor GOD does not so repent him of his deed as the yrefull manne does, whose
sentence of all things is as fixed and steadfast, as his prescience and
foreknowledge is certain. But if Scripture use no such words, yet it does not
insinuate it self familiarly to all kind of men, unto whom, he would it
should be known, and that to fear the proud, stir up the negligente,
exercise those that inquire and seek, and nourishe those that understand, the
which thing he would not do, if his will were not first to bow and incline
him self, and as it were to descend and come down to those which are weak and
feeble.

had respect unto Abel, and to his oblation, but unto Caine and to his offering,
he had no respect.

After that promys was made to Abraham that he should have a child by Sara,
Genesis 8.
he laughed, and so did Sara, Whose laughing our Lord reproved, but not
Abraham's.

We read that when Moses and Aaron showed wonders before Pharao, Exo. 6.
that Pharaos wise men and enchaunters did in like manner with their sorrerye.

Chore and his company had even such censers as Aaron had, Nume. 16.
and perchance of as good metal or rather better: and yet god did not equally
accept their censing.

The Bethsames lifted up their eyes, and spyed the Arc and reioysed, 1. regu.
6.
and offered a burnt offering unto our Lord. And although they seemed to do a
good work, yet our Lord plaged them with a great plague, because they had
seen the Arc, the which they should not have seen.

1. regu. 19.
When Saul was among the prophets, he strypte of his clothes, and began to
prophecye, but it auayled him but little.

Oza put forth his hand to houlde the Arc that it should not faull, 1.
para. 13.
and our Lord smote him incontynently, and there he dyed.

Notwythstandynge it is a very good thing to offer incence unto our Lord, 2.
para. 16.
yet it pertayneth notte to every man to do the same. For Ozias the king of
Judah was smytten with ye leper, because he would burn insence upon the altar
of insence.

Our LORD does reprove by his Prophet Esaias the oblations Esa. 1.
that he him self did institute to be offerde, and that, because of the
wickedness of those that offerde. Why offer ye so many sacryfyces unto me,
says our Lord? Then there follows. Your hands are full of blood.

Our Lord preferred the offering of the widdowe which cast two mites in to the
treasury, Luke. 21.
above the offeringes of the rich men.

Herod desired very greatly to see Jesus. And when he saw him he was
exceading glad, but yet he gate no profit thereby, LuKe. 23.
thoccasion and cause where of was another pitye nor charity, but curiosity and
vanity.

That God at times does tempt and prove man. The.xiii. chapter.
GOD did prove Abraham, and said unto him. Genesis 22.
Take thy son. etc.

Our Lord said unto Moses: behold, Exo. 16.
I will rain bread from heaven to you, and the people shall go out and gather.
There follows, that I may prove them, whether they will walk in my law or no.

And when our LORD spoke with Moses, Exo. 20.
all the people hard their voices, and the sound of the trompe, and saw the
Lamps, the Lyghteninge and the mountain smokinge. And being afraid they said
unto Moses. Talk thou with us. etc. Moses said fear not for GOD is come to
prove you, and that his fear may be in you that ye sin not.

Our LORD did not put all the people clean away from the land of promission,
Iudi. 2.
that through them, Israel might prove whether they would keep his
commandments.

Our Lord left Ezechias to be proved, that all such things as was in his
heart and mind, 4. reg. 20.
at the coming of the king of Babilons messengers, might be known.

It is written, that God, after that Toby was made blind, Tobi. 2.
suffered that temptation to happen unto him, that they which came after
might have an example of his patience,

Judith speakinge of the children of Israel, Iudi. 8.
the which Holofernes thought to destroy, said, that they should call to
remembrance, how their fathers in times paste were tempted, that they in like
manner might be proved, whether they worshypped their God a right or no.

Job for the great tribulations that he suffered, Job. 23.
said of him self. He has proved and tried me, as the gold in the fire.

David desired of our Lord, saying: Examen me O Lord, psalm. 25. psalm. 138.
and prove me. O Lord thou have proved me. etc.

Our Lord Jesus walking on the sea, commanded Peter to come unto him. Mat 14.
But when he saw a mighty wind, he was afraid.

Our Lord said unto Phillippe, whence shall we by bread, John. 6.
that these may eat. This he said to prove him.

Peter said: maruail not that ye are proved as gold by fire, 1. pet. 4.
which thing is to try you.

That man should not tempt God. The.xiiii. Chapter.
ABraham going toward Egypt did wiselye that he confessed not that Sara was
his wife, Genesis 12^ 20.
for if if he had so said, he might have brought both him self, and her into
danger.

And Isaac did in like manner: For if he had done so, Genesis 26.
he in a manner, as says s. Augustine, had tempted our Lord.

The children of Israel tempted our Lord very often in wilderness. Nume. 14.


When the children of Israel were overthrown in battle by the Philistines,
1. regu. 4.
they brought the Arc of our Lord with them into the battle, and it was
taken, and they were smitten with a great plage.

David knew that he was anointed king, 1. reg. 22.23
and that he should reign after Saul, as Samuel had promised and yet he would
not put him self in any ieopardy, but did to keep him self that he might
possible.

When yt an horrible great fish invaded Toby, Tob. 6.
he tarried not that thangel should deliver him, yt which thing he might easily
and quickly have done: but he took the fish by the gil, and drue him to the
dry land.

Ozias had promised and appointed with the people, Iudi. 8.
that he, if there came no healpe after five days were paste, would give up
them selves and the city to Holofernes. Judith said unto the elders of the
city, what are ye, that ye do tempt our Lord? This device or words optaineth
no mercy.

Our Lord was tempted by the devil, that he should cast him self down headlyng
from the pinnacle of the temple. Mat. 4.
But he said to him: Luke. 4.
Thou shall not tempt the LORD thy God. For he might have descended other
ways.

The Pharisees willing to tangle Jesus in his words, Mat. 22.
caused to be demanded of him, whether it were lawful to give Caesar tribute or
no. Jesus perceiuinge their wickedness, said? why tempt ye me, ye hipocrites.

When he had cast out the Deuel, the dombe spoke, certain there were that
tempted him, Luke. 11.
and required of him a sign from heaven.

Peter rebuking Saphira Ananias wife very sharplye, Act. 5.
said, wherefore have ye conspired together, to lie and to tempt the holy
ghost.

Paul in that thing, that by human industrye he could do him self, Act. 9.
looked for no miracle or healpe. And therefore when the Jews laid watch for him
at Damasco, he caused him self to be let down through the wall in a basket.

And when they had him bound with thonges, Act. 22.
and that the Tribune would have punished Paul, he said that he was a Citezen
of Rome. Act. 23.
And again he said that he was a Pharisey, and that to make dissension among
the Jews. Act. 25.
And when he had an unrighteous judge, he appealed unto Caesar.

Of vows. Ca. xv.
Jacob goinge unto his uncle Labans house, Genesis 18.
after the vision that was showed him, vowed a vow, saying. If God will be with
me. etc.

King Arad the Cananite fought against Israel, Nume. 21.
and having the upper hand and victory over them. He took some of them
prisonners. But Israel vowed a vow unto our Lord, and afterward overcame them.

Iepte fought against the children of Ammon, Iudi. 11.
vowed a vow unto our Lord, saying. If thou will deliver the children of
Amon into my hands. etc.

Anna praide unto our lord, and sore weping vowed a vow, 1. regu. 1.
and said O lord of hosts. if thou will give me a man child, I will give
him unto our lord.

Absalon willing to rebel against his father king David, 2. regu. 15
said unto him I will go now to Hebron, and pay my vow which I have vowed
unto our lord. For thy servant vowed a vow, when he was in Gesur, in the
land of Siria, saying: If our lord shall bring me again to Jerusalem, I will
do sacrifice unto our lord.

Asa the king of Judah offered up 2. Para. 15.
those things in the house of our lord that his father had vowed and dedycated
unto our Lord, even silver, gold and diverse other vessel.

And the people reioysed when they were so willinge to make their vows, 1
para. 19.
for with all their hearts they offered their goods unto our Lord. And David
the king reioysed with great gladness.

And the children of Israel and Judah brought in and offered their tithes, 2.
para. 31.
which they had vowed and consecrated unto our Lord.

King Artarerzes commanded Esd^as and the people, 1. Esd. 7.
that they should bring gifts unto our Lord God of Israel, the which they
had vowed and promised our Lord.

All the people after the victory, came to Jerusalem to praise and give
thanks unto our Lord, Iudi. 16.
and they all offered burnt offeringes, their vows and promises.

The men that were in the ship where Jonas the Prophet was, Jonas. 1.
feared exceadingly, doing sacrifices, and making vows unto our Lord.

2. Match. 3.
Heliodorus purposing to spoil the tresuary, and violently to take away such
things as were laid there to be kept, was be the divine power grievously
scourged, and afterward made whole through the prayer of Onyas, he offered
unto god, made great vows, and so returned to the king again.

After that our Lord had, smytten Antiochus with a grievous plague which no man
could heal, 2. Match. 9.
he promised the Jews to garnysh the temple, with great gifts.

Luke. 1.
It seems that the blessed virgin made a vow of her virginite, forasmuch as
she said. How shall this be, seeing I know not a man.

Those Jews made a cruel and a wicked vow, Act. 23.
that coming to the hie rulers said: we with deuocio^ have made a vow, that
we will nether eat nor drink, nor taste any thing till we have killed Paul.

Of Prayer. Ca. xvi.
ABraham most humbly, discretelye, Genesis 18.
constantly and mekely did pray our Lord, to spare the Sodomites.

At some time we must pray our Lord for such things, Genesis 25.
as he has purposed to do. As Isaac made intercession unto our Lord for his
wife, because she was barren. And yet our Lord purposed that she should
conceive and bring forth children.

It is greatly to be thought upon. How thankeful, Genesis 32.
how lowly, and how importune that Iacobbe was in his prayer, saying, Lord I am
not worthy of the least of all thy mercies. And afterward how he sequestrated
him self from his wives and all his familye, and remained there alone in the
night.

Moses prayde our Lord oftentimes, Exo. 7.8.9.10.
that he would remove the plagues from Egypt, and was heard, notwithstanding
that the people were evil.

Moses in the war that the children of Israel made against Amelech, Exo. 17.
did more by prayer, than Joshua by fighting.

The only prayer of the mind does cry and ascend unto God, as it well
appears when our LORD said unto Moses that spoke nothing unto him, Exo. 14.
wherefore cryest thou unto me.

After the adoration made unto the caulfe. Exo. 32.
Our Lord as it appeared, would have utterly destroyed the people, but Moses
by reason of instante prayer abtained their pardone. But yet note, the manner
of his praying, either (quoth he) forgive them their sin: or wipe me out of
thy book.

After Moses intercession and prayer, Nume. 11.
the fire that had devoured the hosts of the murmurers, and those that were
heavy and sorry of their labor, quenched.

Our Lord being even yr^full against the people that demanded flesh in
wilderness, Nume. 11.
granted them their peticion, whereby it appears, that the extudicion and
hearing of man's prayer, is not alwais a sign of divine and godly dilection.

Mary by the intercession and prayer Nume. 12
of Moses was healed of her leprosy

The people being sore afflycted with fiery serpents, said unto Moses^ Nume. 21
pray for us, and he made intercession for the people.

Anna being troubled in her mind prayed unto our Lord, 1. regum. 1.
and wept sore, and vowed a vow, she spoke in her heart, and her voice was not
hard at all.

When the children of Israel should fight against the Philistines, 1. regum.
7.
they said to Samuel. It is necessary that thou pray and cry to our Lord for
us, that he may save us out of the hand of the Philistines.

It pleased not God that the children of Israel should require a king to
reign over them. 1. regum. 8.
And yet our Lord said unto Samuel, hear the voice of the people, in all
that they say unto thee.

Samuel said unto the people, GOD forbid, 1. regu. 12^
that I should sin against our Lord, and cease prayinge for you.

David said, 2. reg. 7.
that he had found in his heart, to pray to our Lord.

David prayed and besoughte God for the child, 2. regu. 12.
and fasted, and went in and lay upon the earth. This was a very good manner of
praying, but David was not then worthy to be hard.

Helias praying for rain, said to his servant, 3. reg. 13.
look toward the seat, for from thence he trusted that some rainy cloud would
arise, but until the seventh time nothing appeared, whereby the instancye and
continuance of prayer is commended.

King Iosaphat smitten with fear, gave him self wholly to pray unto our Lord.
2. para. 20.
For he heard say, that a great multitude of people was coming against him.

Hezechias after he had hard ye king of Assiryans messengers used very good
counsel, 4. reg. 19
when that he sent unto Esaias the Prophet, saying: make thy prayer for the
remnaunt yt are found and left. And the king turned him to pray unto our
Lord. And note there, how faithfully and how prudently he made his prayer.

Hezechias that he might pray the more attentively turned his face to the
wall, iiii. reg. xx.
and prayde our lord, saying, I beseech thee now O Lord remember how I have
walked before thee in truth and with a perfyt heart, and have done that which
is good in thy sight and Hezechias wept sore.

Manasse the king of Judas prayer was very humble, ii. Pa^ xxxi^i
devout, and effectuus, as men may se in the later end of the book.

Who fasted and praide our Lord to have a sure and a right way, i. esd. 8.
and it chaunsed prosperously. And when he gave the king drink, he made his
prayers to God of heaven, Nehe. 1.
and when he should answer to those things that were asked him, he prayde
most humbly.

When Tobi had heard his wives evil and naughtye communication, Tob. 2.3
he took it heuely, and with tears began to make his prayer.

When Sara the daughter of Raguell had heard the great reproach and rebuke of
her maiden, tobi. 3.
she went into an hie chamber of her house, and continuinge iii. days in
prayer, she besought God with tears, yt she might be delivered from that
rebuke.

Tob. vi.
Raphael the aungel, that the devil might have no power upon Toby the younger,
warnd him, that when he had taken Sara to his wife, and was come into the
chamber, that he should with hold him self from her three days, and give his
diligence unto nothing but unto prayer with her.

Iudi. 4.
When the children of Israel heard of the power of Holofernes, they cried unto
our Lord. But Eliachim the hie priest put them in remembrance, how that Moses
overthrew Amalech that trusted in his might and power, not with weapons, but
with holy prayers.

Iudit. 8.
Judith did trust greatly in other men's prayers, and therefore she purposing
to go to Holofernes, said unto thelders, pray ye unto god, that he will
stablishe, and bring my counsel to good end. And after follows: Do ye
nothing else but pray unto our Lord for me.

Judith. 13
In like manner^ when she should smite of Holofernes head, she made her prayer
with tears standing before the bed.

And when Esther should speak unto king Ahasuerus, Esth. 4
she said to Mardocheus. Gather all the Jews together that may be found,
and fast ye and pray for me: but how deuoutlye and how humbly they praid,
and how Mardocheus prayed for him self and the people. It is written in
the.xiiii. Chapter of Esther.

The prayer of Jeremy was of great reputation with God, Ihere. 11.
when our Lord said unto hi^, pray not for this people.

Azarias standing in the mydst of the furnace, Dani. 3.
praid thus. Blessed art thou o Lord God of our fathers.

Daniel for all king Darius act and decre, Dani. 6.
left not of kneling down upon his knyes to pray unto the Lord like as his
manner was to do before time, three times a day. See now how precious and how
profitable a thing he esteemed it to pray unto our Lord.

Daniel perceiving the time of the Captiuitye to be complete, and at an end,
prayde the more instantly for the people that were in captivity. And note how
mekely and how fervently he makes his intercession and prayer. Dani. 9.


When Susanna perceived that she lacked all human aid and counsel, Dani. 13.
she made her recourse to the help of prayer, and her prayer was heard.

Jonas prayed unto our Lord, out of the fyshes bellye, Jonas. 2.
and said, in my trouble I called unto our Lord, and he heard me.

The congregation were ready gathered to fight, 1. Match. 3.
to pray, and to make supplication unto God for mercy and grace.

When that Judas Machabeus should give battle with Gorgias he made his prayer
and said, i. Mac. iiii.
blessed be thou O savior of Israel. i. match. Vi.
In other.ii. principal battaylles we read not that he prayed, The one was
against king Antiochus, and then he wanne not but departed his ways. i. Mac.
ix.
The other was against Bacchides and Alchimus, and then he was slain in the
battaille.

i. match. xi.
Ionathes perceiving that al his company, except a few, left him fightinge
against strangers, he rent his clothes, and praid, and afterward obtained
the victory.

The Jews being in tribulatyon, prayed unto our Lord. The priests having on
them their priestly stoles and vestimentes fell down before the aultare and
called upon God, ii. mac. iii.
which had made a law concerning stuff given to keep that it might be safely
preserved for such as deliuerd it to be kept. And all the women held up their
hands toward heaven and praid.

Onias the hie priest praid for Heliodorus that was grievously scourged by God
for spoiling of the temple, ii. mac. iii.
and our Lord restored him to life again.

Judas Machabeus and they that were with him, iii. Mac. viii
praid and besought our Lord to deliver the^ from wicked Nicanor: and though
he would not do it for their sakes, yet for the couenaunte yt he made with their
fathers, and because they called upon his holy and glorious name.

The wicked Antiochus praid unto our Lord, of whom he should have obtained no
mercy. 2. Match. 9.


Nicanor and they that were with him, 2. Match. 15.
drue nie with shaumes and songs: but Judas and his company with prayer and
calling upon God. They buckled together, with their hands they smote, but with
their hearts they prayed unto our Lord, and slew no less the^ 35. thousand
men: for through the present help of God, they were gloriously comforted.

Mat. 8.
The Leper had a short, a profitable, and an humble manner of praying, Luke. 5.
the which knelinge before our Lord did worship him and said, Mark. 1.
master, if thou will thou can make me clean.

The Centurion used as it were by a certain insinuation, Mat. 8.
the like manner of prayer, Luke. 7.
when he said: Master, my servant lies sick of the palsy.

Ihon. 11.
And also Martha and Mary for Lazarus that was dead and buried.

Our Lord at times will be prayed for that, Luke. 10.
that he purposes to do, pray ye the Lord of the harvest to send forth
laborers into his harvest. Mat. 9.
Then there follows immediatelye. Calling together. etc.

And when the people were sent away, he went up into a mountain to pray
alone. Mat. 14.
Whereby we are taught, that when we inte^d to pray, we should fie the company
of man, lest we should be troubled.

Our Lord and savior in his holy Gospels, Mat. 6.
has taught us to pray by word of mouth, saying: Thus shall ye pray. Our
father. etc.

Men ought always to pray, Luke. 18.
and not be weary.

Also our Lord has animated us to pray by his promise. Luke. 11.
Ihon. 14.
Ask (says he) and ye shall have. Item, what soever ye ask in my name, that
will I do.

He has likewise informed and taught us to pray by his example. Mat. 14.
For he that might command, would pray.

And specially he did the same. Mat. 26.
for ye persecution of this Passion being at hand, he prayed, and warned other
to pray, saying: watch and pray.

When Mary Magdalen obtaind forgeuenes of her sins of our Lord saying: Luke.
7.
Thy sins are forgeuen the, we read not that she used any loud prayer, but
that she wept only, where by the efficacye of the inward desire appears
without any vocal or loud prayer.

Our Lord does induce us to instant and continual prayer by thexample of one yt
went to his friend at midnight. Luke. 11.


Luke. 18.
And by thexample of a widow, the which desired with great importunity of the
wicked judge to avenge her.

And to instruct us to pray with hu^mility and without pride, Luke. 18.
or any aua^cement of our selves. Our Lord induc^th thexample of the proud
pharisy, and the lowly and humble Publicane.

Act. 1.
After our lords assention into heaven, the Disciples returned unto Jerusalem,
and they al continued^ with one accord in prayer and supplication with the
women and Mary.

Thapostles being minded and willinge to choose one of the disciples in Judas
place, Act. 1.
appointed two, Joseph, and Mathias, and when they prayed, they said: Thou Lord
which know the hearts of al men, show whether of these two thou have chosen.

In the primitive church, al faithful people continued in the Apostles doctrine
and fellowship, Act. 2.
and in breaking of bread, and in prayers.

Peter and Ihon went up together into the temple at the ninth hour of prayer.
Act. 3.


And as soon as the disciples had prayed, the place moved, Act. 4.
where they were assembled together, and they were all filled with the holy
ghost, and they spoke the word of God boldly.

The Jews stoned Steven, calling on, Act. 7.
and saying: lord Jesus receive my spirit. And he kneled down, and cried with
a loud voice, saying: Lord, lay not this sin to their charge.

Peter and Ihon prayed for them of Samaria, Act. 8.
yt they might receive ye holy Ghost: then laid they their hands on them, and
they received the holy Ghost.

Saul being prostrate upon the thearth, and profitably execated and made blind,
Act. 9.
stood up again, and coming into Damasco, and began to pray, and was three
days without meat or drink.

Cornelius the Centurio was a devout man, and one that feared GOD wtal his
household, which gave much almose: Act. 10.
and prayed God always: whereby he disposed him self to aproche and come to the
faith. And therefore it follows. Thy prayers and thy almoses are come up into
remembrance before God.

Peter was kept in Herodes prison, but prayer was made without ceasing of the
congregation unto god for him. Act. 12.


When the holy ghost had said: separate me Barnabas and Saul, Act. 13.14
for the work whereunto I have called them. It follows. And when they had
fasted and prayed, and laid their hands on them, they let them go. Again
there follows. That they did marvelous much good.

Peter went up unto the hiest part of the house to pray, Act. 10.
about the vi. hour, that he being far from those that were beneathe might
pray the more devoutly.

When Paul went to pray, he met a damsel possessed with a spryte that
Prophesied, whom Paul deliuered^ commaundinge the spirit in the name of Jesus
Christ to come out of her. Act. 16.


Paul departing from Achaia and his brethren, Act. 20.
after a little communication, and a few godly words, he kneled down, and praid
with them al, and they al wept very sore.

When Paul had praid in the temple, he was in a trance, Act. 22.
and saw our Lord Jesus, saying unto him. Make haste and get the quickly
out of Jerusalem.

After that Paul had prayed, and had laid his hands on Publius father being
sick of a fever, Act. 28.
and of a bloody flixe, he healed him.

Paul the Apostle, monished, These. 5.
that we should pray continually the which thing he him self did most
diligently. Romans 1.
For to the Romans he says, with out ceasing I make mention of you in my
prayers.

To pray is to diffycyle and so heard a thing, Romans 8.
that Paul says, that he is not fufficiente nor hable to do it.

We know not that we pray as we should pray, 2. these. 3.
and therefore Paul does often and most humbly desire other men to pray for
him. Brethren (says he) pray ye for us.

Paul caused prayers to be made, to avoid that was evil, and also to obtain
those things that are good: of ye first he says thus, romans 15.
I beseech you brethren that ye help me with your prayers, that I may be
delivered from the unfaithful. And yt he believed that he was helped by other
men's prayers, he says.

Our Lord has delivered us from so great dangers and pearels. Of the second,
that he desired to obtain goodness by other men's prayers, 2. cor. 1.
he says. Praying for us, that God may open unto us ye door of vtteraunce,
that we may speak the mystery of Christ. And in a another place he says.
Coloss. 4.
Brethren pray ye for us, that the word of God may have passage, 2 Thessalonians. 3.
and be glorified.

Paul prayed for other men, and that he might be fruteful unto them. romans 1.
With out ceasinge I make mention of you, praying always in my prayers, that
by some mean a prosperous journey by the will of God, might fortune me to come
unto you.

And to Timothe, without any ceasing or intermission, 2. timo. 1.
I make mention of thee in my prayers night and day, desiring to se thee.

And also he prays for the Thessalonians, that God would call them to the way
of health, 2. these. 1.
saying: we pray always for you, that our God will make you worthy of this
calling.

And for the Philippians, that they may profit and encrese from that that is
good to better, Philip. 1.
saying: And this I pray: that your love and charity may increase more and
more.

And also that the Collossians might have ye fullness of divine knowledge, col.
1.
saying: we cease not to pray for you, and to desire, that ye might be
fulfilled with the knowledge of his will.

The Apostle S. James, says, that the prayer which is made for corporal and
bodily health, Iaco. 5.
avails. The prayer of faith shall save the sick. And also for eternal
salvation, the which is the very true health. Pray one for an other, that ye
may be saved, for the prayer of a ryghteous man avails much.

Of the observation and keeping of the Sabbath day. Capit. xix.
THe observation of the Saboth had his original beginning of that, Genesis 2.
that is said and written in Genesis. God blesses the seventh day, and
sanctified it, because that in it, he reasted from al his work.

And the children of Israel gathered in the wilderness on the.vi. day a
double quantitye of Manna. Exo. 16.
Because that on the Sabbath they should reast from all work.

And among all the ten commandments, Exo. 20.
there is only a reason given of thobseruay^on of the Saboth, because that
among carnal men, it seemed to have little reason. And this precept is very
often times found in the law, to the intent that man should diligently observe
and keep it, and labor to get and obtain the true reast.

And on the Sabbath day there were offered two lambs, Nume. 28.
and upon other days but one except in solemn feasts and kalendes. And
that, to declare, yt in festiual days men should honor god more reverently and
aboundauntlye then other days.

The man that was taken gathering of sticks upon the Saboth day, Nume. 15.
was by Gods commandment stoned with stones of all the people.

Nehemias saw some treading wine presses, 2. Esd. 13.
and bringing of burdens to be sold upon the Saboth day, and he rebuked them
as breakers of the Sabothe.

The gentiles which held with Antiochus appointed to fight upon the Sabbath
days against certain Jews that were fled out of Iewry, 1. match. 2.
but they casted not one stone at the^, nor made fast their preuy places: but
said, we will die all in our innocencye. But yet it is to be observed and
noted, that notwythstandynge that in this thing they showed a Deuotyon toward
Gods commandment, yet inas much as they perceived afterward that thereby
Gods people might be scattered and lost, they took better counsel: saying.
What soever he be that comes to make battle with us upon the saboth day, we
will fight against him, for why to fight for the defense of man's life, or for
the law of God, is no servile work or labor.

Judas Machaheus and his company fought against Nicanor and his host, 1.
match. 7.
and slew 5000. men, and put the rest to flit^. But yet they followed not the
chase, because it was ye day before ye saboth.

Nicanor thought withal his power to strike a field upon a Sabbath day.
Nevertheless the Jews that were compelled to go with him, 2. match. 15.
said: O do not so cruelly and vnkindlye, but halow the Saboth day.

The Pharisees said unto the Disciples that did pluck and eat ye ears mat.
12.
of corn, 1. regu. 21.
ye do that which is not law full to do upon the Sabbath day. But the Lord
said unto them, have ye not read what David did. etc. Then follows. The
son of man is also LORD even of the Sabbothe day.

We do read that our savior did many miracles upon the Sabbothe day, Mat.
12.
as it is manifest through out all the Gospel, and for that, there may be
assigned three causes. First, to show him self to be the Lord. Mat. 12.
The second, to open the true understanding of the precept and commandment,
for me^ ought not to cease from all works upon the Saboth. Luke. 6.
Whether is it lawful on the Sabbath days to do good, or to do euel, Luke. 12.
to save ones life, or to destroy it. The third that he might edifye and
profet all that saw him and hard him.

When Christ had healed the woman which was bowed together, the ruler of the
Sinagoge disdayned, Luc. 13.
because that he had healed on the Sabbothe day, and said. There are six
days, in which men ought to work, in them come that ye may be healed and not
on the Sabbath day. But the Lord answered him, and said. Thou hipocrite, does
not each one of you on the Sabbath day lose his Ox or his Alfe from the stal,
and lead him to the water? And ought not this daughter of Abraham, whom Satan
has bound, lo 18. years, be loosed from this bond on the Sabbath day? And
when he thus said, all his adversaries were ashamed, and all the people
reioysed on all the excellent deeds that were done by him.

The holy women which had prepared sweet odours, Luke. 23.
to anoint our lords body, kept the sabbath day so strictly, that on that they
would not anoynte so precious and holy a body. So they rested the Sabbath
day, according to the commandment.

God, Act. 13.
and the prophets. The which are read every Sabooth day.

Of blasphemy against God. Ca. 23.
THe Israelitish woman's son was stoned to death by Gods commandment,

because he blasphemed the name of our Lord.

Hely said unto his sons. 1. regu. 2.
If one man sin against an another, our Lord may be pacified and pleased: but

Nathan the Prophet did agrauate the sin of David, 2. regu. 12.

to blaspheme his name.

thy hand, and ye shall know that I am the Lord.

Of Gods precepts and commandments and of the observation and kepinge of
them. ca. xxiiii.
OUr Lord gave unto our first parent Adam a lyte and a easy commandment to
be fulfilled. Genesis 2.
Saying. Thou shall eat of every tree of the garden, but as touching the tree of
knowledge of good and evil, thou shall not eat of it. But he kept this
commandment but evil, and therefore he fell into a great and grievous pain and
punyshement.

Notwithstanding the commandments seem at some times to be of lyte and
slender matters, Genesis 2.
yet they ought and with no small diligence to be observed in as much as the
transgressors are grievously punished. For our Lord said unto Adam: In what
day or hour soever thou eatest of the tree of knowledge of good and euel, thou
shall dye the death.

Noe did every thing, even as the Lord commanded him. Genesis 7.


When the people of Israel should receive the Commandments of God, Exo. 19.
they were commanded to be sanctyfyed. Go unto the people and sanctyfy them
to day and to morrow. And therefore he commanded ye children of Israel, to
make them gardes of yellow sylke in ye quarters of their garments, Nume. 15.
to have a contynual remembrance of the celestyal co^mandeme^ts.

Our Lord when he made Iosue ruler over his people, Iosu. 1.
gave him a special monytyon, of the medytatyon and obseruatyon of his law
and commandments.

Balaam the sorcerer said unto Balach the king: Nume. 23.
Told not I thee, saying. Al yt the Lord commands, that must I do? Behold
now, what reverence this evil man had to gods commandment?

Joshua omytted nor mynyshed no word of all that our lord commanded. Iosu. 11.


Saul the which was specyallye chosen, 1. regu. 15.
was utterly rejected and cast away for the trangressyon and breakyng of Gods
commandment.

David instructynge and teaching Solomon his son, 1. Para. 22.
the which should raygne after him, said: Then thou shall prosper, when thou
fulfillest the statutes and laws, which our Lord gave to Moses.

After the ordinance of Ioiada the bishop, 2. Para. 23.
they brought out the kings son, and put upon him ye crown and gave him in
his hand, the law that was to be kept, and made him king.

Syrus king of Persia, and Monarch of all the world, 1. Esd. 1.
was not ashamed to say. Our Lord God of heaven and earth has commanded
me to build him a house at Jerusalem.

Our Lord eue^ complaining does say. The commandments of Ionadab the son of
Recchab, the which he commanded his children to keep, and that they should
drink no wine prevailed and were better kept then mine. Iere. 35.
For they obeyed their fathers commandment, I have spoken unto you, and yet
have ye not been obedyent unto me.

Susanna putting her life and good name in pearell and danger, Dani. ^3.
judged it better to fall into the hands of man, then to forsake and leave the
laws of God.

There were two women accused to have circumcysed their sons, 2. Match. 6.
who^e when they had led round about the city (the babes hanging at their
breasts) they cast them down headlinges over the walls.

Eleazar an aged man sustained grievous pains of the body, 2. Match. 6.
and at length he was put to death, because that he against ye law of god would
another eat swines flesh, nor yet fain or dissemble that he had eaten it.

For the law of god the vii. brethren with their mother suffered grievous and
intolerable pains under Antiochus. 2. Match. 7.


Other creatures that obey the lord do induce us to observe his commandementes,
2. regu. 24.
of good angels there is no doubt, the which are his mynysters, doing his will
and his word. Of evil angels. 1. Para. 21.
He commanded the evil sprite to go out of the man. Luke. 8.
He commanded the Ravens to feed Helias, and they did so. 3. regu. 17.
And the Psalm does say generallye. He has given them a law, which shall not
be broken. Fire and hail, Psalm. 148.
snow and Ise, wind and storm fulfill his word. Job. 9.
He commands the Sun, and it ryseth not.

The parents of Ihon the Baptist walcked so in all the law, Luke. 1.
ordinances and iustyfications of our Lord, that no man could find faut

Of obedience and disobedience. Ca. xxv.
GOD willing that man being in the state of innocence should live under
obedience, Genesis 2.3.
bound him with precepts and laws, and punished him right sore and
grievously, living disobedyently.

Noe spedely obeyed our Lord in althinges that he, Genesis 7.
at the instant time of the flood, commanded him.

Notwithstanding that Gods commandment of the circumcision was a grievous and
an unwont thing, Genesis 17.
yet Abraham made no procrastinatyon, nor no delay to fulfill and accomplish
the same? For even in ye self same day that god commanded it, he fulfilled it.

Abraham without any stop or delay offered up his only son in a sacrifice.
Genesis 22.
Behold and consider his marvelous and wonderful obedyence.

Joseph did spedely obey his father yt sent him to his brethren, Genesis 37.
although he had accused them, where upon he (and not without a cause) might a
feared to have gone unto them.

Moses obeyed our Lord that made Exo. 3.4.
him the captain and guide of his people. But mark yet with what difficultye.
For he excused him self five times.

The children of Israel promised great obedience, Exo. 24.
saying. All the words which our LORD has said, will we do. But yet
afterward they did the contrary in their deeds.

The children of Israel walkyng in the wlldernes at Gods commandment pitched
their tents, Nume. 9.
and at his commandment they took the^ down.

Also the children of Israel were afraid to ascend and to go up into the land
of promise, Nume. 14.
when God commanded them, but when God forbad them, they strove to go up, but
it was to their pain.

Many of the children of Israel that went to war against the commandment
of God and Moses, Nume. 14. Nume. 31.
were ouerthrown of a few: but when they fought by obedience and commandment
a few overthrew a multitude and wan the victory.

In as much as Achan transgrest ye commandment of Joshua, the people were
overcome in battle, Iosu. 7.
and all Israel stoned him with stones.

Although David was anointed king by Samuel, 1. regu. 17.

notwithstanding he was elected and chosen above al his brethren.

Our lord foretold Solomon, 3. regu. 9.

if he turned away, 2. Para. 7.

Of holy scripture. Ca. xxvi.
WE ought to have great reverence unto holy scripture, Exo. 31.
the which God him self did write, deliver and teach.

Moses returned from the Mount bearing two tables written with the finger of
God. Exo. 31.


Our Lord Jesus does say, that he was sent to Euangelice and preach, mat. 10.
and he sent forth his disciples to do the same.

If it may be said then, that the old law was given Moses by god, by the
means of angels, as says the Apostle, and S. Steven does testify the same.
Act. 7.
Ye have (says he) the law of God, by the ministration of angels. The reast
of the old Testament was given by the inspiratyon of the holy Ghost, as says
S. Peter. The scripture came never by the will of man. 2. Pet. 1.
But holy men of God spoke, as they were moved by the holy ghost. The new
Testament does contain the words and deeds of the Lord Jesus Christ in the
Gospelles, the words of the Apostels in the Epystels and in the Apocalipses,
the deades of the Apostles in the acts. Christ very God and man, spoke part
of the Gospel by him self, and the holy ghost, and by him other words, the
which the Apostles and the Evangelists by him instructed did speak. They were
all filled with the holy ghost, Act. 2.
and began to speak with diverse and other tongues.

A wise man seeks out the wisdom of them of the old time, and exercyseth him
self in the prophets. Eccle. 39.
As though he would say. A wise man must exquire and seek the wisdom of wise
men, but specially he must give his diligence to the scriptures of ye prophets.

Notwithstanding that Ionathas the hie priest and the elders of the Jews were
occupied in matters of war, 1. Match. 2.
yet they were unto the Spartianes, under this manner: But as for us, we read
no such matter, for why we have the holy book of scripture in our hands to our
comfort.

And our Lord answering by scripture, defended his disciples against the
Pharisees. Have ye not read (quoth he) what David did when he was an ho^gred?
Mat. 12.


Our savior being tempted of the devil, Mat. 4.
answered by scriptures, and by the auctoryte of scripture confounded him: And
he said that the scripture was fulfilled at his coming. This day is this
scripture fulfilled in your ears. LuKe. 4.


Our Lord gave great auctoryte to the old Testament, when he said Till
heaven and earth pass, Mat. 5.
one jot or one title of the law shall not escape till all be fulfilled. And
the scripture cannot be losed or broken. And the new Testamente is of no less
aucthoryte, Joan. 10.
but rather of more then the old: Of the which our Lord sayth^ Mat. 14.
Heaven and earth shall pass, but my words shall not pass.

Our Lord oftentimes overcame the hie priests, mat. 21.
Scribes and Pharisees even by Scriptures, the which reproved him.

Our Lord reproved the Saduces of ignorance, mat. 22.
saying. Ye do err, not knowing the scriptures:

men.

red the prophet Esaias sitting in his charette, is much commended and praised.

Paul coming unto Berrheham, entered into the Jews Sinagoge Certain of them

Of good exhortation, and predication of the word of god. Cap. xxvii.
CAine being admonyshed by the exterior voice of God, Genesis 4.
left not of his pretenced iniquitye. And by this it is patent and manifest,
that the exterior exhortation without the interior, is of very little and small
efficacy

The just man Lot did mekelye admonyshe and exhort the Sodomites, saying. Nay
for gods sake my brethren do not so wickedly. Genesis 19.
Do not this evil unto who^ they answered, very contumaciously get the hense.
Thus it appears, that peruers people are hardly cured and corrected.

It happened and chanced well with Jacob, Genesis 27.
for as much as he agreed unto his mothers exhortation and counsels.

Ruben hearing the wicked words of his brethren against Joseph, Genesis 37.
said: Let us not kill him, nor shed his blood, and Judas gave counsel
not to slaye, but to sell him, that so the less hurt might ensue and follow.

Moses sister persuaded Pharaos daughter even well, Exo. 2.
that an Hebrews woman might be called to nurse ye child.

that he should appoint and orden mean judges for the people.

Nabals blud.

Abner gave good counsel to Asaeli that followed after him, 2. regu. 2.

But because he would not hear him, he slew him.

The old men gave Roboam Salomons son good Counsel, 3. regu. 12.

sorts of men.

Of evil Spirits. Ca. xxxii.
Evil spirits are said to be our Lords, 1. regu. 16.
because they are in gods power, and what so ever they do, they do it by God.
The evil spirit of God vexed Saul.

The devil killed Saras Raguels daughter vii. husbands, Tobi. 3.8.
but yet by the coming of Raphael the good angel was eiected.

Satan had even so much power upon Jobs cattle his house wherein his
children did eat, Job. 1.2.
and upon his body, how much the divine prouydence did suffer him to have.

The evil sprite made the man fearce and cruel. Mat. 8.
And also he makes a man unclean, for those ii. demoniakes, or possessed with
devils were out of measure fearce, Luke. 8.
and dwelt and lay in graves. And the devils desired to go into the swine,
not into Lambs. One of those ii. was more famous then the other, he ware no
clothes: he abode in no house but in graves, he was bound with chains, and
kept with fetters, and he brake the bands, and was carried of the fend into
wilderness.

This euel sprite makes a man both deaf and domme, Mar. 7.
and when the spirit takes him, he knocks and teareth him and he fometh and
gnasheth with his tethe and pineth away, LuKe. 9.
Mar. 9.
and often times he casts him into fire and water, to destroy and lose him.

Our Lord refused the laud and praise of malign spirits. LuKe. 8.
Hold thy peace (quod he) and come out of the man. Mar. 1.


Our Lord did forbid his discyples to rejoice that the evil spirits were
under them, Luke. 10.
and subdued unto them, as though they should not esteem that thing very greatly.

A certain damsel possessed with a sprite ye prophesied, Act. 19.
cried out many a day after Paul and his fellows. But Paul being heavy
therefore, turned about and said to the sprite, I command the in the name and
virtue of Jesus christ yt thou come out of her, and he came out the same hour.
And note yt Paul would not that the doctrine of truth should be confirmed by
the spirit of deceitfulness and falshode.

Certain of the Jews took upon the^ to call over the^, which had evil sprites

we adjure you by Jesus whom Paul preaches. And the evil spryte answered and

evil spryte was, ran on them, and overcame them, and prevailed against them,
so that they fled out of that house naked and wounded

Of the immortality of the reasonable soul. Ca. xxxiii.
FOr as much as it is said of Abraham, that he was put to his people, Genesis 25.
it is supposed that he had people in a another world, that is, men, which lived
well as he did.

We have the like saying of Isaac. He was put unto his people. Genesis 35.49.
And of Jacob.

And when Jacob believed that his son Joseph was dead, Genesis 37.
he said, I will go down into hell unto my son mourninge. So then, he believed
that he was there in spryte.

Iosephes brethren having in will and mind to say, that one of their brethren
was dead, said. We are xii. brethren, Genesis 42.
the sons of one man, the youngest is with our father, and one no man wotteth
where he is.

Our lord appearing unto Moses in a bush, Exo. 3.
said, I am the God of Abraham Isaac, and Jacob. etc. by this our savior
proves the ressurection of the dead. Mat. 22.
He is not a God of the dead says he, but of the living.

It is said of Chore and his company, that they went down alive into hell,
Nume. 16.
and the earth closed upon them, and they pearyshed from among the
congregation. By this it appears that the evil, as touching their souls do
live in hell.

If Saul had surely believed that Samuel had been extincte and dead as
touching his soul, 1. regu. 28.
he would not have desired him to have been reuyued and called again.

When that David's servants, maruailed why he wept not for his young son
that was dead, he said, I shall go to him rather the^ he shall come again to me.

When that David's servant, meruailed why he wept not for his young son that
was dead, 2. regu. 12.
he said, I shall go to him, rather then he shall come again to me.

When Absolon was hanged, and thrust through with iii. spears, 2. regu. 18
David be wailed and lamented him mournfully. And s. Augustine in his book de
doc. chri. says. That David bewaild not the lack and death of his son. But
because he knew to what pains that adoulterous and Paracide soul should be
drawn unto. But for his other son that died an Innocente, and for whose
sickness he was sore afflicted, 2. regu. 12.
he reioysed.

3. regu. 17.
Helias praid for the reuiuification of his hosts child, saying. O Lord my
God, let this childs soul come into him again.

Oftentimes we read in the books of the kings, 3. regu. 14.
he was laid a sleep with his fathers. The which thing by no means may be
understood or spoken of brute beasts: 4. regu. 13.
and therefore there by it is proved that they live after their death, and that
here after they shall arise again, as it appears in those that sleep.

It is manifest and open by Thobias words which he spoke rebuking the
folishnesse of his kinsfolks, that the soul lives after that it is separated
from the body. Tobi. 2.
We are, says Toby, the children of holy men, and look for the life, which
God shall give unto them that never turn their be lefe from him. And
afterward in his oration and prayer he says. Tobi. 3.
O Lord, deal not with me according to thy will, and command my sprite to be
received in peace.

Our Lord gave Job double of al ye ever was his. Tobi. 42.
And at length he gave him vii. sons, and iii. daughters.

The preacher (after the mind of s. Eccle. 11.
Gregory in the last of his Morales) spoke expressly and plainly, saying. Let
the dust be turned again unto earth, from whence it came, and the spryte
shall return unto God, which gave it.

By those words that the dampened do say in hell, they declare and show,
Sapi. 5.
that the good as well as the evil do live in a another world.

Thus it is written even literallye of Nabuchodonozor king of Babylon Now that
thou art laid down to sleep that is in death, Esai. 14.
there come no mo up to hew us down. Hell also beneathe trembles to meet
thee at thy coming. And after there follows. Thy pride is brought down into
the deep of hell. And many mo things ar written there, by the which it is
euidente that he pearished not utterly, but that his soul went down into hell.

When that they counseld Eleazarus to feign and dyssemble him self to have
eaten of the flesh of the sacrifice: 2. Match. 6.
he said. Though I were now delivered from the torments of men, yet should
not I escape the hand of almighty God, nether alive nor dead.

One of those seven brethren, said. 2. Match. 7.
Those things I possess and have from heaven, but now for the law of God, I
despise them, for my trust is that I shall receive them. Of him again.
Likewise it is clear and manifest by the mothers words and other, that they,
as touching the soul believed not that they should pearish.

Razias taking his own bowels, threw them upon the people, 2. Match. 14
calling upon our Lord and ruler of the earth, and spirit to reward and restore
him this again, and so he dyed.

Our savior warninge his Dysciples, the which he sent abroad, Mat. 10.
said unto them. Fear ye not them which kyl the body, but are not able to
kill the soul. But rather fear him, which is hable to destroy both soul and
body into hell.

That thing which our Lord does show of the rych man and Lazarus seems to be
no parable or symilitude, Luke. 16.
but a manifest hystorye. And so it appears that the souls both of the good
and evil be immortal, and receive after the separatyon from the body, even
as they deserved being in the body.

Our Lord by the ensample of the unjust steward that made him friends with his
masters goods, Luc. 16.
does conclude: saying: make you friends of the unrighteous Mammon, that when
ye shall have neade, they may receive you into everlasting habitatio^s. The
which saying was of none effect, if the soul after the separation from the
body, or after the death of ye body, had no receptacle or place to be received
unto.

Blessed saint Steven had a devout and a right opinion and faith of the soul,
Act. 7.
the which when they stoned him, said, Lord Jesus, receive my spryte.

It appears manifestlye by the words of that excellent doctor Paul tha^ the
soul does live after it be separated from the body. 2. Cor. 5.
We know (says he) that if our earthy mancyon of this dwelling were
destroyed, we have a building of God, an habitation not made with hands, but
eternal in heaven.

Philip. 1.

ELiezer Abraham's servant did the message committed unto him, Genesis 24.
by his master very faithfullye, when he went for Rebecca to Bathnals house.

Jacob served his uncle Laban faithfully, when that he keeping his sheep by day
was consumed with heat, Genesis 29.31.
and by night with frost.

Joseph showed him self faithful unto his master, Genesis 39.
in that he would not touch his wife. And in his counsel that he gave unto
Pharao: Genesis 41.
and in such service as he exhibited and did for him.

Rachab the harlot did faithfullye with the spies which Iosue sent: Iosu. 2.6.
and likewise Iosue afterward used her faithfully again.

Although the Gabaonites had deceived Iosue and the children of Israel, Iosu.
9.10.
