defended them against their enemies.

Ionathas did faithfully disclose his fathers ire and wrath unto David, 1.
regu. 20.
and as much as lay in him, excused him, and afterward comforted him.

Abiathars father being slain by the occasion of David, 1. regu. 22.
I am, says David, the cause of the death of all the souls of thy fathers
house. Abide with me, and fear not. For if any seek my soul, he shall seek
thine also, with me thou shall be in sauegarde.

David would not smite, nor lay his hands upon Saul his Lord and king. 1.
regu. 24.
Notwithstanding he was euel, and did persecu^e him, and yet if he had would,
he might twyse have slain him.

The harness bearer of Saul was a great sign and token of fidelitye, 1.
regu. 31.
and yet he did but indiscreetly, when that he, seeing his master was dead,
would live no longer, but fell upon his sweard, and died with him: what ought
we then to do for our Lord that was crucified for us?

The men and inhabitours of Iabes in Galaad, 1. regu. 31.
showed them selves faithful to Saul their Lord, notwythstandinge he was
evil and wicked, when they reverently buried him.

Urias the Hethite would not live in delight and pleasure, 2. regu. 11.

Of the love that man ought to have to his neighbor. Cap. xli.
CAyne was grievously reprehended of our Lord, Genesis 4.
and punished because he did wickedly against his brother, and said that he
was not his brothers keeper.

Note how diligently and carefully Abraham prayde our lord, Genesis 18.
that he would spare the Sodomites, the which thing was a great sign and
token of love.

Moses had so great dilection and love to his neighbors, exodi. 32.
which were his subjects, that in his prayer to God, he said, either forgive
them their sin, or wype me out of thy book.

Moses did wyshe in his prayer, that our Lords people could prophecy, Nume.
11.
notwithstanding that his honor should seem to be deminished thereby.

Moses would have no greater dominion then he had, Nume. 14.
and yet our lord promised him it. Such was his love toward his neighbors
whom he ruled.

1. Corin. 3
And as a builder building. As a wise builder have I laid the foundatyon.

And yet nevertheless it may be said that Paul by other ways and means
showed him self to be a most fervent lover of his neighbors. Because he did
many things for them. For he either sustained them, or e^sse he gave them, and
procured for the power that he had not to give them, of those that had it, and
Paul him self does testify that he counseled and did for the vtility and
profit of his neyghbors, saying. Act. 20.
These hands have ministered unto my necessities, and to them that were with
me. For it is more blessed to give, then to receive: and al though it was a
work of supererogation, considring he might have received somewhat of them, yet
he did it to spare those he preached unto. I am ready says he, 2. Corin. 12
to come unto you, and yet will I not be chargeable unto you for I seek not
yours, but you. Secondarely he took nothing, that he might cut of from the
Pseudapostles the occasion of gloryfying. In all things I kept my self so that
I should not be chargeable to any man, 2. Cor. 11.
and so will I keep my self. What I do, that will I do, to cut away occasyon
from them, which desire occasion, that they might be found like unto us, in
that wherein they rejoice. And again he procured that thereby he should have
the greater reward. We have not used this power to receive any reward of you.
1. Cor. 9.
What is my reward then. Uerely that when I preach the Gospel, I make the
Gospel of Christ fre. Paul procured also of the congregatyon of Achaia, to
dystrybute and give to the pore that were in Iewry, and therefore he caused
collectyons, 1. Cor. 16. 2. Cor. 9.
to be gathered, and induced the faithful effectuously to the same. Item he
that sows lytle^ shall reap little.

And he distributed unto his neighbors the word of God, wherewith he
plentifullye abounded. Ye and gave him self to be profitable unto his, we
would have dealte unto you not the gospel only, but also our own souls
because ye were dear unto us. ii. These. ii
And again he says, ii. Cor. xii.
I will very gladlye bestow, and will be bestowed for your souls.

Furthermore Paul even with his own body did marvelous things to convert his
neighbors to the faith and to spiritual health by preaching, disputing, and
iournyinge from Damasco to Arabia and Jerusalem, and to Antioche. And then by
the commandment of the holy ghost, with Barnabas he went from Antioche to
Cipers, and from thence they sailed by Cicill, and came to Persida. Iconium,
Lycaoniam, and ordained prestes and elders in every congregation. And after
that they had done much good, they returned to Antioche. Afterward Paul
purposing to visit his brethren unto whom he had preached the word of god, he
took Sila with him, and went to Siria and Cilicia, and from thence to Phrygia
and Galatia, and came to Mysia, and after that being called, he sailed into
Macedonia. And when he had done much good at Thessalonia, and in many other
cities of that regyon, he went to Athens, and there he disputed with certain
curious Philosophers. And from thence he went to Corinthum, and there he
converted much people to our Lord. And then he took his iourny to Ephesus, and
entered in to the sinagoge and dysputed with the Jews. And from thence he went
to Cesaria, Act. xvii.
and from Cesaria he came to Antioche, and after he had tarried there a certain
time, he took his iourny toward the country of Galatia and Phrigia, and
confirmed and stablished all the disciples. And when he had wandered over all the
hye parts of the country, he came again to Ephesus, and tarried there two
year, disputing of the kingdom of God, and did so much, that all they that
dwelte in Asia both heathen and Jews did hear the word of God. From thence
he returned by Macedonia, Troyade and Miletum, and passing by many other
cities and Isles, he came to Tire and from Tire he took his journey by
Ptolomaidem, and Cesaria, and came from thence to Jerusalem. And there the
Jews took him, drew him, bet him, and falsely accused him, before diverse
judges, and manifestlye grieved, was constraind to appele unto Caesar He was
delivered unto the captain, and after the ship was broken, and many other
pearyls, he being bound with chains, came to Rome, and there being given to
preaching and teaching, purposed to go into Spain. Behold now how he loved
those, for whose sakes he suffered such and so many pains and pearils. And
Paul says, we do all things dearly beloved for your edifying. ii. Cor. xii.


Also the signs of love appear, when a man will sustain and suffer that is
grievous for his friends sake. For it is written. Thou shall not be ashamed to
salute or defend thy fre^d: and if any evil or hurt chance unto the through
him, Eccle. 12
sustain and bear it.

Out of these forsaide words, it is open, that Paul suffered wonderful
things for his neighbors profits. 2. Timo. 2.
I suffer (says Paul) all things for the electes sakes, that they might
also obtain saluatyon. Of this look in the title of tribulation, for there
thou shall find many things as touching this matter.

It appears by S. Ihons words, that he had great love to his neighbors.
For his mouth spoke, of the haboundance of his heart, when that he so often
repeated charity, as it apeareth in his first Epistle. Capit. iii.iiii.

Of Envy. Capitu. xlii.
Through envy of the devil, Sapi. 2.
came death into the world, for when he saw that man was in a happy and good
estate, and that he might ascend to that he fell from, he tempted man, and
overcame him.

Cain moved with envy, slew his brother Abell, Genesis 4.
because he saw that God accepted his brothers gifts, and not his.

It is written of Isaac, that GOD blessed him, Genesis 26
and that he waxed rych. And therefore the Palestines enuyed him. And so it
appears, that prosperity occasyonally does cause the evil to hate and to envy
many.

Rachel that was baren, envied her sister which was full of children. Genesis 30.
Behold how that envy spares not even those that are nigh of kin.

Iosephes brethren did most cruelly hate him, Genesis 37.
because they saw that their father loved him more then all his brethren, and
because of his dremes that he rehearsed unto them, and note what mischefe came
of it.

When that two men prophesied in the host, Nume. 11.
Iosue as though he enuyed the thing, said: master Moses forbid them. And he
said, enuyest thou for my sake? would God that all our Lords people could
prophecye, Nume. 11.
and that our Lord would put his spirit upon them.

Mary Moses sister, and Aaron spoke against Moses, Nume. 12^
saying, our Lord has not only spoken by Moses. Has he not spoken also
by us? whereby it appears that the envious spares another friend, nor kinsman.
For Moses was their brother, and through him they had received great honor.

dyspleased him.

Envy was very far from John the Baptist. John. 3.
For when his disciples came unto him saying, that Christ did baptize, and all
men come to him. He answered. The friend of the bridegroom. Which stands and

Some of the Jews that had seen our Lord revive Lazarus, John. 11.

The hye preastes and pharisees even through envy committed so cruel a deed,

as to crucify our lord, for Pilate said that he knew that for envy the hie

Then the chief priest rose up, and all they that were with him, Act. 5.

When the Jews heard Steven speak, Act. 6.7.
their hearts claue a sunder, and they gnashed with their tethe, being right

^^oued and stirred up the city against them.

Of peace and concord. Cap. xlviii.
Genesis 1.
IN the beginning god made all other beasts double, that is male and female.
But he created man sole, and of him are all other procreated and made, and that
to commend the unite of peace and concord in man.

Riches and abundaunce of temporal things, Genesis 13.26.
are oftentimes the matter and occasion of strife and debate, as it appears in
Abraham's and Lots herdsmen, and Isaac and the shepherdes of Gerare.

Men do gladly make peace and frendshyppe with such as be of great might
and power. Genesis 16.
And therefore Abimelech came to Isaac, because he saw him prosper.

Sumtimes a man must give place, and avoid the fury or hastines of his better.
Genesis 17.18.
As Jacob did departing from his brother Esau, until his fearsnes and wrath
was swaged.

The Gabaonites hearing what Joshua had done at Ierico and Hai, Iosu. 9.
came unto him, and made a good peace and agreement with them.

When Phinees and the other legates that were sent unto the children of Iosu. 22.
Ruben, had heard their excuse, they were appeased, and gladly received their
answer.

Although Absolon had done to 2. regu. 18.
wickedly against his father yet David more desired peace then the death of his
son, for he said. Is the young man Absolon safe.

Notwithstanding that David was holy, 2. regu. 7.
and such a one as pleased god, yet our lord would not that he should build
him a house, but that Solomon his peasible son should enjoy and be honored,
and have that privilege.

Our lord is much to be lawded and praised, when he gives his people a
peasable and a quiet estate, 3. regu. 5
as was in Salomons time, the which said. The lord my god has given me
rest on every side, so that there is neither aduersarye, nor any evil plage.
Then there follows, blessed be our lord.

Good and blessed men have love and amite one to a another. 3. regu. 14.
But, the evil fight against the good, and other that are evil. As there was
war contynually between. Roboam and Jeroboam.

It was declared and shewde unto Helias that our lord was not in the mighti
strong wind, 3. regu. 19.
nor in the earth quake nor in the fire. But in a small still voice, that is in
tranquilite and peace.

And the people blessed and thanked all those, 2. Esd. 11.
that were wyllinge to dwell at Jerusalem.

Ionathas sent ambasidoures unto Bachides for to make peace with him, 1. Match.
9.
and yet the self Bachides was capytane of the hooste, in the which Judas
Machabeus Ionathas brother was slain.

King Demetrius sent letters unto Ionathas with loving words and praised him
greatly: for he said we will first make peace with him, 1. Match. 10.
before he bind him self with Alexander against us: else he shall remember
the evil that we have done against him, his brother and his people.

The cause of the peace that was in Onias time, 2. Match. 3.
was his wisdom and goodness, and the goodness of his subjects.

After that Judas Machabeus had overthrown Lisias, 2. Match. 11.
he wyllinglye and gladlye made peace with him. For he perceived that the
Hebrews being defended by the healpe of almighty God, could not be overcome.
Wherefore he sent them word, and promised that he would consent to all
things, which were just and reasonable, and to make the king their friend.

Our Lord would us to have so much peace and concord with our neighbors,
Mat. 18.
that he said unto Peter, that we should not forgive our brother, if he sin
against us, till seven times, but seuentye times seven times.

The Angels in our Lords nativity brought tidinges of peace and commanded
them to have peace among them selves, Luke. 2. Luke. 10.
John. 14.
and that they should show it forth. Luke. 24.
Forther more he leaft them peace, and after his resurrection he offered them
peace.

He that desires to keep peace, and to have the quietness of mind, must
abstain from discursions and troubles of the mind, John. 11.
and at sometimes cease from that, that is honest and laufull. For when Martha
heard that Jesus was come, she went and met him. Mary sat still at home, nor
moved not thence until she was called of our Lord by her sister, although
that Mary parauenture was not ignorant of our Lords coming when that
Martha knew it before.

How great that the goodness of peace is, it may be pondred by Paul that
discrete judge: the which most diligently in all his Epistles does wyshe it
to all those that he writes unto: except in his Epistle to the Hebrews, in
the which for certain causes he nether sets to his name, nor premytteth
any salutation. Note yet, that when he says peace be unto you, he premytteth
grace. Saying. Grace be with you and peace. Roma. 1.
Where by it is manifestely understood, that true peace cannot be had,
without the grace of god. Esa. 48.
And therefore Esaye says.

As for the ungodly they have no peace.

Of unite and common consent. Capi. xlix
De. Ci li. 12. Capi. 22.
GOD made mankind of one man, to commend and declare unto men, how pleasant a
thing the unite of many is unto him. Whereupon Saint Augustine does say. Man
was made one, but not left alone. There was never thing that humayne nature
spoke of, so commodius for mankind so full of discord through vice, so given
to feloshippe, so natural, against the vice of discord, other to be taken
head of, if it be not, or to be helped and healed if it apeare, as the
remembrance of our first parent, whom god would creat alone that of him
many other should spring, and that by this admonition, a concordiall unity
might be observed and kept in many.

The people of Israel was of one consent and mind in the desarte, Exo. 19.
and willing to receive the law. For after they had hard of Moses the words of
the law, they answered all with one voice, all that our Lord has said, we will
do.

The people, to make and perform the work of the tabernacle of our Lord,

and the holy uestmentes of the ministers, did bring in and offer with most

so revenge and punish the flagitious dede^ committed against the Levites wife

And all the people gathred them selves to gether, 2. Esd. 8.

When Achior had disclosed all things that Holofernes had said, Iudi. 7.

After the death of Judas Machabeus, al his friends came together, 1. Match. 9.

After that the people had heard Simons words, 1. Match. 13.

After the assention of our Lord, Act. 1.
all the disciples continued with one accord in prayer and supplication with

All that believed kept them selves together after they had received the holy
sprite, Act. 2.
and had all things commen, and continued dailye with one accord in the

When the disciples had heard that the creple was healed, and of Peter's and

and said, Lord which have made heaven and earth. etc.

After that Ananias and Saphyra his wife were terriblye punyshed at Peter's
word, Act. 5.
great fear was through out all the country. And they were al together with one
consent in Salomons porch.

And the multitude that believed were of one heart, Act. 4.
and of one soul. Nether said any of them, that ought of the things which he
possessed was his own, but they had all things common.

Of discord, strife and debate. Ca. l.
Envy moved the first discord among men, Genesis 4.
as betwixt Cain and Abell, because that Caines works were malign and evil,
and his brothers good and just.

The substance of Abraham and Lot was great, Genesis 13.
and they could not dwell together, and so there fell a strife between ye
herdme^ of Abraham and Lot.

The five kings of the Sodomites served and were subject unto Chodoriamor xii.
year, Genesis 14.
and in the xiii. year they rebelled, and departed from him. And so there was
war between four kings against five. In the which war Lot was taken, and
recovered by Abraham.

The inhabitours and men of Sodom did compass the house about, Genesis 19.
in the which, two angels in the likeness of me^ war lodged, for they would
have known them, and they preased sore upon Lot because that faithfully he
defended his gestes.

There was strife and debate between the heardmen of Gerar and Isaacs, Genesis 26.
for the possession of sheape, of Oxen, and a mighty household.

Jacob fletinge away was wroth, Genesis 31.
and said to Laban. for what trespace or offense art thou thus angrye with me
and have searched all my stuff.

By the occasion of Dina Jacobs daughter whom Sichem Emors son Iere. 34.
did rauyshe, and forced, a great dyscorde arose between Jacobs sons, and
the inhabitoures of that Country.

Moses upon a certain day, saw two Hebrews that strove together. Exo. 2.
And he said unto him that did the wrong? Wherefore smitest thou thy fellow?

After that the Children of Israel were gone out of Egipte, Exo. 17.
and were paste the red sea. Amalech came and fought with them in Raphidim.

Oftentimes the children of Israel did strive against Moses in the
wilderness. Genesis 16.17.
First for lack of drink. And again when they had one kind of meat, Nume.
21.
they desired a another. And when they lothed Manna, they calde for flesh. Also
they came together against Moses and Aaron at the waters of contradiction and
strife, Nume. 20.
where they did chide and murmur against our Lord and Moses.

Between Abimelech Gedeons son, and the men of Sichem, the which had made
him king wrongfully, Iudi. 9.
was great dyscorde, so that they began to detest him, and to rebel against
him, and he ouercomde them.

There arose astrife between those of Ephraim and Iephthe, Iudi. 12.
for as much as Iephthe going to fight aginste the children of Ammon would
not, as they said call them.

There was so vehement a discord and battayl in Gabaa Benjamin and iudi. 20.
the Tribes of Israel for the Levites wife that they of the Tribe of Benjamin
were utterly all slain, except. 5. hundred.

After that David had slain the Philistine. 1. regu. 18.
Saul was wroth and angry with, David, because he was most commonly praised.
Wherefore Saul looked a side on David from that day forewarde. Nor no man
could from that time mollify his heart, but needs he must persecute him.

There was long debate and strife between the house of Saul, 2. regu. 3.
and the house of David. But David. Waxed stronger and stronger, and Saul
continually weaker and weaker.

There was to great and to dishonest a dissension and discord between Absolon
couetinge the kingdom and David his father. 2. regu. 18.
At the last yet Absolon that moved the same, was hanged.

When David returned to Jerusalem, the children of Israel were troubled and
vexed because that the Jews, 2. regu. 19.
they being not calde there unto, brought him again.

Two women did strive be ^ore king Solomon for a child, 2. regu. 3.
the which they both would have had.

After the death of Solomon, the people desired his son Roboa^ to use and to
handle them more courteously. 3. regu. 12.
But because he answered the^ churlishly and hardly, ten of the Tribes left^
him and made Ieroboa^ their king by ye occasion whereof, there was sore wars
between the kings of Israel and Judah.

There was a strife among the disciples, which of them should seem to be
the greatest, Luke. 22.
but it appears by that, that follows that such contention and strife
pleased not our lord.

John. 6.
The Jews strove among the^ selves saying, how can this fellow give us that
flesh of his to eat.

And much murmuring was there of our lord Jesus among the people, John. 7.
for some said, he is good, other said nay, but he deceives the people. There
follows. There was dissension among the people.

After that Cornelius was christened with all his house, Ac 1.11.
the Apostles and brethren that were in Iewry hard that the heathen had also
received the word of god. And when Peter was come up to Jerusalem, they that
were of the circumcision contended against him saying wherefore wentest thou
into men uncircumcised.

When Paul and Barnabas preached, and did many miracles in the city of
Iconium, Act. 14.
the multitude of the city was divided, and part held with the Jews, and
part with the Apostles.

Certain men which came down from Iewry, Act. 15.
taught the brethren, saying, except ye be circumcised after the manner of
Moses, ye cannot be saved. So when there was risen discencio^ not a little unto
Paul and Barnabas against them, they determined that Paul and barnabas, and
certain other of them should goo up to Jerusalem unto the Apostles and Elders
about this question.

Act. 15.
By the occasion of John, whose sir name was Mark, whom Paul would not take
to the work of the gospel, there arose a dissension between Paul and
Barnabas, so that they departed asonder one from the other yet al was for the
fortheraunce of the gospel.

Paul preaching and doing many miracles at Ephesus, Act. 19.
there arose no little a do about the way of our lord for a certain man named
Demetrius a silver Smyth which made Silver shrines for Diana, was not a little
beneficial unto crafts men. etc. And all the city was in a rore, and in great
confusion.

When certain of the Jews saw Paul in the temple, Act. 21.
they moved all the people, and laid hands on him, criynge. Men of Israel
help. And all the city was moved, and the people swarmed to gether.

When Paul had cried out in the counsel. Act. 23.
Men and brethren, I am a pharasei, the son of a pharasei. Of the hope and
resurrection of the dead I am judged. And when he had so said, there arose a
debate and a dissension between the Phariseis and the Saduces, and the
multitude was divided.

Of prudency and discretion. Capitulo.liii.
ABraham coming into Egypt, did wisely and warely, Genesis 12.20.
as touching his wife, for he cloked the truth, and yet affirmed no falshode,
saying. She is my sister. He did the like, when he came to Abimelech.

And Abraham did prudently separate him self from Lot, Genesis 13.
because their herd men should not strive together.

Abraham discretelye while he yet lived, Genesis 25.
did divide and give every child his portion, least that they, after his death
should strive and he at debate.

Rebecca did wiselye enstructe her son Jacob, Genesis 27.
how he should obtain and come by his fathers blessing, and prudently she
caused him to depart from those parties, until his brothers fearsnesse were
swaged.

Jacob by craft did even very well begyle Labans craftiness, Genesis 30.
when Laban denied to give him competente wages for his service.

Jacob did prudently, that he, when he should meet with his brother, Genesis 32.
sent him Presents, and when he divided his Substance, least that he,
even at one brounte should lose al, and put such things as he loved best in
danger.

Genesis 41.
Joseph spoke prude^tly before Pharao expounding the dream unto him and giving
him counsel against the famine that was to come.

Genesis 44.
Joseph did warely and wiselye deprehend and accuse his brethren, and put them
in fear.

Iethro gave Moses good counsel, saying: Exo. 18.
provide thy self men of power, and such as fear God, true men, and such as
hate covetousness.

Or ever Moses invaded the land of promise, Nume. 13.
he sent spies thither to consider the state and condition thereof.

The spies that Iosue sent, lurked and wisely kept them selves close, Iosu. 1.
until they that sought for them were returned to their own again.

Iosue used great policye and wisdom, when he laid awaite unto the town of
Hai, Iosu. 8.
and afterward made as though he had fled his way.

The Gabaonites thinking by craft and subtlety to beguile Iosue, by his
discretion were brought into seruytude and bondage. Iosu. 9.


Phinees and other messengers that were sent to the children of Ruben, Iosu. 22.
spoke discreately unto them, and with wise communication appeased them.

Ahud bringinge a present unto Eglon king of Moab, Iudi. 3.
craftily deceived him.

Gedeon did smite and destroy the host of his enemies, Iudi. 8.
the which being without care, did cast no peryls.

Iephthe like a wise man did signifye Iudi. 11.
by messengers unto the king of the children of Ammon, that he did wrong to
war against him, but yet afterward he made an vndyscreate vow.

Iepthe did wyttely perceive who were Ephraites, Iudi. 12.
and who were Galaadytes, by the pronou^syng of this word Schibbolech, that is
an ear of Corn, when they said Schybbolech. For they could not so pronounce
it.

The children of Israel fighting against the Beniamites by policy and craft
feigned them selves to fly, Iudi. 20.
and by that means drew them out of the City, and utterly destroyed them.

Saul when certain men despised him, 1. regu. 10.
and said, how can this manne healpe us, dissembled the matter, and made as
though he had not heard them.

It was a point of great wisdom when Dauyd being armed with Saules armor,
1. regu. 17.
proved whether he could so go against Goliath, or no.

David went out to all things, whythersoeuer Saul sent him, 1. regu. 18.
and behaved him self wisely.

David in the presence of Achis fained him self mad, 1. regu 21.
and as though he had been in a furye, so to escape from him.

Abigail did wiselye pacify Dauyd being angery with Nabal her husband. 1.
regu. 25.


2. regu. 12.
Nathan goinge about to reprove the Prophet Dauyd of his excess and fautes
done to Urias and his wife, took and used wisely the manifest parable of the
rich manne, that took a sheep from a poor man.

Ioab used a wise cautel, 2. regu. 17
when that by a wise woman he caused Absolon to be revoked.

A wise woman of Abel, 2. regu. 20.
returned Ioab from the obsidion and seige of the city.

Bersaba, hearing that Abdonias would raygne for his father, 3. regu. 1.
spoke wisely unto David for her self, and her son Solomon.

Salomom desired of^ god discreation and wisdom, 3. regu. 3^
the which thing pleased god exceadyngly, and with wisdom, he granted him
many other things.

Solomon judged wisely between two w^men that conte^ded and strove for one
child. 3. regu. 3.


King Roboam answered his people very hardely, 3. regu. 12.
and forsakinge the good and discreate counsel that his sad and old
Senators gave him, he spoke after the counsel of young me^ and did unwisely.

When Achab king of Israel should be rebuked, 3. regu. 20.
a certain man of the children of the prophets discretely proponed a parable
of a man that was commended, and evil kept, and saved. By the which the king
might easily perceive his sin and wickedness.

Iehu did studiuslye and prudentlye when he feigned that he would do reverence
and honor unto the prophets and preastes of Baall. 4. regu. 10.
And yet afterward he slew them, and destroyed Baals altar.

Ezechias king of Judah, 4. regu. 18.
did studiously and discreately forbid that his people should make no answer
unto blasphemus messengers of the king of the Assirians. For it is not
expedient for faithful people to have unfaithful disputations with and
against litigious persons.

used him self both warely and wisely.

Tobias beleuinge that he should dye shortelye, Tob. 4.

Judith showed great wisdom in her words. Judith. 11
And all Holofernes servant marueled at her wisdom and said one to
another. There is not such a woman upon earth, in bewtye contenaunce, and
discreation of words.

Mardocheus required Esther with great wisdom to help the Jews. Esth. 4.
Saying, if thou hold thy peace at this time, the Jews shall be otherwise
delivered, and thou and thy fathers house destroyed. And who knows whether
thou art come to the kyngedome for this causes sake.

God gave unto Daniel and his fellows connyng and learning in all scripture and
wisdom: Dani. 1.
but to Daniell specially he gave the understanding of visions and dreams.

Daniell did expound Nabuchodonosors dreams most wisely. Dani. 2.4.13.
And afterward we do read, although it chanced before, of two old preastes
the which had given, as he most wyselye perceived, false testimonye and
wytnes against the Innocent Susanna.

The vii. brethren with their good mother, 2. Mac. 7
by their words, which they had one to another, and to the tirant: declared

Nevertheless Judas commanded certain men of arms to be set, and to wait

It appears by the communication that the blessed vyrgin had with the aungel,
that she had great discresyon and wisdom. Luke. 1.
For she casting in her mind, what manner of salutatio^ that should be, said,

And when the child Jesus of xii. year old tarried at Jerusalem, and was
found in the temple sit^ynge in the midst of the doctors, LuKe. 2.

understanding, and answers.

Our Lord commended the unjust steward, Luke. 16.
because he had done wisely.

Our Lord very well deluded the curious interrogacion of the priests and
elders askinge him, Luke. 20.
by what authority he did those miracles, he said. I also will ask you one
thing. From whence is the baptime of John?

When Paul and Sylas were put in prison, the Magestrates sent the next day
after, Act. 16.
and commanded that they should be losed, Paul said wisely. They have beaten
us openly vncondempned. Notwithstanding that we are Romans, and have cast
us into prison, and now would they send us away privily?

When the city of Ephesus was sore moved and in a confusion, Act. 19.
Paul did wisely and humblye agree to the counsel of his friends, that he
should not prease into the common hal. Where also appears the wisdom of the
Scribe that pacified the people being so moved, and how he sent every man to
his own house.

And when the Tribune had commanded that Paul should be bea^en and scourged,
Act. 22.
Paul said unto the Centurion that stood by him. Is it lawful for you to
scourge a Romain and vncondempned? Then they which should have punished and
examyned him, departed from him.

When Paul purposed to sail out of Greece into Syria, Act. 20.
and heard say that the Jews laid wait for hym^ he wisely returned through
Macedonia, nor refused not the company of his brethren which were of diverse
cities.

Paul understanding that the one part was Pharisees. He cried out, I am a
Pharisey. And certain of the Phariseis stood up, and fought for him. Act. 23.
And after when he hard say that some of the Jews had made a vow, not to
taste nor eat nothing until they had slain him, he caused ye to be showed to
the Tribune, yt which sent him with armed men to Felix ye ruler of Syria.

When Festus the president would have sent Paul, at the instaunce of the
Jews, to Jerusalem. He wiselye perceiving their malice, Act. 25.
appealed to Caesar.

Of deceit and subtlety. Capi. liiii.
Genesis 3.
IT is manifest that the deuel in the form of a Serpent was the first master of
al craftines, lies, and deceitfulness, the which being more subtle, then all
other beasts, deceived the first woman, he would not board the first man,
because he knew that he had more discreatyon then the woman.

Laban Jacobs father in law, went very oftentimes about to deceive him, Genesis
29.30
now in his wife, now in his wages. But our Lord in the fraud and guyle of
those that would have circumue^ted him, was with him and aided him.

When Laban searched Jacobs household stuff, Genesis 31.
and came to search Rachels tent, she craftily deluded his careful searching.

rape of their sister Dina, Genesis 34.
counsaild Sychem, the people, and inhabytors of the City to be circumcised,

Jacobs Children would have deceived their father, Genesis 37.

utterly to extirpate ye children of Israel, and destroy them in Egypt, and by

Jeroboam thought in his heart, 3. regu. 12.
now shall the kingdom return to the house of David, if this people go up

Because that Satan could by no means deny before our Lord Iobes virtues, he

When Paul and Barnabas were at Listra, Act. 14.
and in so great favor, that men would have done sacrifyce unto them as

but lyingly they said. These men trouble our city, and preach ordinances,

The Jews malitiouslye did purpose to desire the Tribune that Paul might be

as though they would have known something more perfectly of him: but many

That it is a pearillous thing not to agree to good counsel. Ca. lvi.
THe angels that appeared unto Lot, gave him this good counsel, that he
should depart from Sodom, and take his sons in law with him, and that they
should not look behind them, but save the^ selves in the hill.

The which Lot said unto his sons in law that they should be going, but
he seemed to them as though he had mocked. Genesis 19.
And therefore Lotte sons in law, that would not depart from that wicked
people, did pearyshe with them. And his wife that looked behind her, was
turned into a pyllare of Salt. And Lot him self that would not, after the
Angels counsel by and by ascend up to the mount, did trespass and sin
with his own daughters.

father, being a frayde to offend him.

The lesinge or lie that ye mid wives made to Pharao, unwilling to slay ye

It is never lawful to lie, to tell the truth is always lawful. 1. re. 16.

do that.

Of Couetiousnes. Capitu. lxxiii.
IN that, that Cain slew his brother, Genesis 4.
because he saw his brothers goods increase, may be noted great avarice, and
a great desire of money.

We read that Cain was the first that builte any city, Genesis 4.
and not Abel. For good holy men have hear no contynuynge city, Heb. 13.
but they seek one to come.

Because of the great substance that Abraham and Lot had, they could not
inhabit and dwell together: Genesis 13^
And their herdsmen began to strive one with a another.

The abundaunce of temporal goods, Genesis 13.
is oftentimes the occasion of great sin, as it is enident by the Sodomites
which were of all other sinners the wurst.

After that Isaac grew to be rich, his shepeherdes and his neghboures began to
braule and chyde. Genesis 26.


Judges and prelates ought to hate auaryce more then any other vice. Exo. 18.
And therefore Iethro spoke notablye of Judges. Thou shall seek out those that
hate covetousness.

There are few preastes in these days that forbid or let the superfluite of
oblations, Exo. 36.
as they did that were rulers over the works of the tabernacle.

Balaacs messengers went unto Balaam having money and rewards in their
hands, Nume. 22.
and so he was corrupted with covetousness.

The tribe of Ruben and Ead. And half the tribe of Menasses, Nume. 32.
because they had great substance of cattail, would not goo over Iordane.
But were content for their portion to inhabit and dwell in the countrei apt
and meat to f^de and bring up their cattayle.

Achior seduced by covetousness, took of the excomunicate things of I^richo.
But for that lucre and gain, Iosu. 7.
he had and sufferd great loss and damage.

Dalida for money that was promised her of the philistians, Iudi. 16.
delivered Samson her husband unto them.

It is written of Samuels sons, that they turned a side after lucre, 1.
regu. 8.
and took rewards, and perverted the right.

Covetousness seems to be the chefest cause or occasion that Saul was reproved
for, 1. regu. 15.
I mean the cupidite that he had to Amalechs pray. For Samuel said unto him,
wherefore haste thou not harkened unto the voice of our lord, but have turned
to the pray, and haste done that is wicked, In the sight of our lord.

1. regu. 25.
but for Abigail his wifes sake, he had welnye lost both his substance, and him
self to.

After that Nabuchodonozor had gotten the victory of Arpharat the king of

by and by he occupied and subdued, all other kingdoms.

Judas Machabeus said unto his people and companions, 1. Match. 4.

Ptolomi the king of Aegipt slaundren Alexander his son in law, 1. Match. 11.

Simon of the tribe of Benjamin styrde Appolonius and king Antiochus against

Menelaus through the money that he promised Antiochus obtained the hie
prichode. 2. Match. 4.
And at length by menes of the golden vessel that he stale out of the Temple,
the which he gave Andronicus, he caused Onias to be slain. And being

sentence of death against his accusers. And the self Menelaus through the

When that certain Jews at Machabeus ^. Match. 10.
commandment had besieged two towers in the which their enemies were, 2.
Match. 10
certain strangers entreated for money let some of them escape, the which,

After that the war against Gorgias was ended, Judas Machabeus and his
company came, 2. Match. 12
to burye the bodies of them that were slain. Under the cotes of certain
Jews that were slain, they found money and Jewels of ydols, which thing
was forbidden the Jews by the law. And therefore men believed it to be the
cause that they were slain.

The young manne that inquired of our lord how he might have eternal life,
Mar. 19.
had great and rich possessions, and therefore when he hard the counsel
of perfection, he went a way so^ye.

The preastes wyllinge and desiring that the people should oftentimes offer,
mat. 21.23.
did suffer that such things as might be offered, should be sold in the
temple. And for this cause the goulde of the Temple was calde more holy then
the temple, and the gift that was upon the aultare, to be of more reverence
then the altar it self.

The covetousness and cupiditye of gain seems to be the Pryncipall motion,
mat. 26.
why that Judas betrayed our Lord. For he says what will ye give me, and I
will deliver him unto you.

By money the kepers of our lords sepulcher were corrupted, mat. 28.
and said falsely, that our Lord by night was stolen away by his disciples.

Our Lord Jesus the true lawyer, Luc. 12.
would not meddle with the diuisyon of the worldly heritage, notwythsta^ding
that he was required, but said, who made me a judge or a deuider over you?

Our Lord against those that heap up temporal goods, Luc. 12.
and thyncke that they shall many years delight and have pleasure in them,
does propounde the Symylytude of the rich man, whose ground brought forth
plentiful fruits.

Luke. 16.
Our Lord against these rich glottons, that use these precious and delicate
garments, which are straighte and neady to releaue and healpe the pouertye of
their neighbor, does put forth the parable of the rich glotton. And note,
that it seems not to be a parable, but an history. Again note that if he be
so punished that gave not his own proper goods, what shall become of them,
that steal other men's?

Luke. 14.
The biers of Oxen and Farms, that is the biers of things moveable and
immovable excused the^ selves, that they could not come to ye great supper
unto the which they were invited and called. For by such things men are
oftentimes withdrawn from the celestial glory.

The covetous Pharisees, hearing our Lords monitions, Luke. 16.
and that they should make them friends of the unrighteous Mammon, laughed him
to scorn.

The avarice of Ananias and Saphira, the which kept away parse of the price of
the land, Act. 5.
was most terribly punished.

Certain crafts men, which had a damsel possessed with a spirit that
prophesyed, Act. 16.
whom Paul delivered of the Deuell, perceiuinge that they had lost their gain
and lucre, caught Paul and Silas his fellow, and brought them to the rulers
and officers, saying, and accusyng them, that they troubled the city, and
preached unlawful obseruaunces and customs. The magestrates rentinge their
clothes, commanded them to be beaten and to be cast into prison, and to be
kept with all diligence.

Paul being at Ephesus, and doing there many miracles, Act. 19.
a certain manne named Demetrius, a Silver smith which made silver shrines
for Dyana, was not a little beneficial unto the crafts men, whom he called
together, and said, that Paul had persuaded and turned away much people,
saying, that they be no Gods which are made with hands but deuels, and has
so trouled the City, that it is al in a rore and full of confusion. And they
rushed into the common hall, with one assente, and caught Gaius and Aristarcus
Paul's companions.

When Paul was with Felix the president, Act. 24.
being bound and of the Jews accused as a seditious and a pestiferous person,
Felix hoped money should have been given him of Paul. Wherefore he called him the
oftener and commoned with him. But in as much as it came not so to pas, he did
not quite him, but left him bound to Fest us his successor.

Of Poverty. Ca. lxxiiii.
Genesis 32.
WE read not that Jacob had either beast or man when he departed from his
parents, and went to his brother Laban, but that he went over Jordan with his
staff. And at a certain time being disposed after the Sun was down to
reast him self, 28
he took a stone and put it under his head, and laid him down in the same
place to sleep.

Moses k^pt the sheep of Iethro his father in law, Exo. 3.
priest of Madian, where by it appears that he had no sheep of his own, that
kept other men's.

Ruth the Moabite had no great store of richesse, Ruth. 2.
when she went a glening the ears that the reapers left behind them, the
which pertayned unto the pore.

Saul being content with one ladde, 1. regu. 9.
went for to se^ke his fathers asses. And Saul not long after said unto
Samuel, that his kindred was the least of all the kynreds of the tribe of
Benjamin.

David was the least of all his brethren, so that when Samuel came to annoint
one of Isais children David was in the pastors, 1. regu. 16.17.
nor he was not called at ye beginning, as though he had been of no reputation,
and afterward his brethren being in the host, his father sent him laden
with vitayles unto them.

Helias suffered great penury when he prayed the widow of Sarept to give him a
morsel of bread, 3. regu. 17.
and a little water.

The children of the Prophets did live under Elizeus in great poverty, 4. regu.
4.
the which had but a little bread, and unsavory pottage.

Anna Tobias wi^e went dailye to the weauing work, Tobi. 2.4.
whereby it appears that they were but pore, which could not have their loum
i^ their own house. And Tobias said unto his son, my son be not afraid,
truth it is, we lead hear a pore life, but great good shall we have, if we
fear God, and depart from all syn, and do well.

The children of the Rechabytes build no houses, Iere. 35.
sow no seed, plant no vine, have no vineyardes, drink no wine, but did
dwell in tents.

Nabuharadan left the rascal people, and those that had nothing to dwell
s^il in the land of Judah. Iere. 39.
He spared the pore, but he slew the mighty and rich, or else he led them as
prisonners and captives unto Babylon.

We have an ensample of poverty in the Lord our savior, Luke. ^.
the which was born of a pore mother, and nourished of a poor carpenter,
semelye fed, wrapped in cloutes and not in furs, laid in a maunger, and
afterward when his glorious mother was churched, his parents offered in the
temple, the offringe of the poor. And anon after Joseph fled with the child
and his mother into Egypt. Mat. 2.
And when the child was xii. year old, he abode still in Jerusalem unknowing to
his father and mother: Luc. 2.
And so it appears that they had no great family to associate and serve the
child.

Jesus going about from town to town, Mat. 8.
had not where upon to lay his hed^ and therefore he says. The foxes have holes,
and the birds of the air have neastes, but the son of man has not where to
reast his head. John. 19.
And for this it maketh^ that he hunge bare upon the cross.

The disciples, for the most part, were chosen out of the porest sort, Mat. 4.
Iho^ and James did mend their nets, Mar. 1.
and did wash them. Luc. 5.


In our lords sermon that he made in the mount, the commendatio^ of poverty,
as though it were the foundation of the spiritual building, Luc. 6.
Mat. 5.
is first placed and spoken of.

Among al other Christ's miracles, this is written that the pore receive the
glad t^dinges of the Gospel. Mat. 11.
For before the coming of Christ, it was not wont to be so.

Our Lord said unto the young man that asked him how he might come to
everlasting life. mat. 19
If thou wylt be be perfect, go and sell all that thou have, and give to the
pore. And our lord does promise a marvelous remuneration and reward to those
that leave and forsake any thing for his names sake.

Of that famous and notable Lazarus, which was carried by the aungelles into
Abraham's bosom, Luc. 16.
the Scripture alleges no other work of righteousness or cause of his glory,
but because he received pain in this mortal life, and therefore God in another
life would comfort him.

The poor and feeble were brought into the great supper of our Lord, Luc. 14.
yea, and certain, as it is r^d there, were compelled to come from the hie
ways and hedges.

In the primative church all that believed were together, Act. ^.
and had all things commen, they sold their possessions and goods, and
parted them to all men, as every man had need.

Peter said unto the crepell that asked his alms, Act. 3.
silver and gold have I none. etc.

Paul taking his leave of the faithful of Achaia, Act. 20.
said among other things, I have desired no man's gold, silver, or vesture,
as ye know your selves: for these hands have ministered, 1. Cor. 4.
unto my necessities, and to them that were with me, we honger and thyrste, and
are naked. etc.

Of Fortitude. Cap. lxxvii.
WHen Abraham saw that Lot his brothers son was taken, Genesis 14.
he took his servants born in his own house with other, and set upon the
four kings by night, that had taken him. And after he had pursued, and
smitten them, he brought Lot again withal his substance, and all the people
of Sodom.

The pureness of the conscience makes a man both sure and bold, Genesis 31.

for what offense followest thou so after me, and haste searched all my stuff?

and yet there perished not one of the children of Israel.

Deute. 31

must go and lead this people into the land.

When Iosue went against thinhabitors Iosu. 8
of Hai he was in the front of the hoaste compassed with the aid and strength

Fortitude (as Cicero does say) is a preconsiderate susception and taking upon

Saint Augustine says thus of Paul. Aug. libro. de. ci^i. dei. 14. Ca. 9.
That behoueable says he, and strong man, that labored more the^ all the
other disciples, that did glory and rejoice in his infirmities, that blessed
man Paul (I say) Christ's Champion, whom he taught, for whom he was in
bonds, with who^ he was crucified, in whom he was glorious in the sight of
this world, to whose honor he was a spectakle, both to Angels and manne
that gladlye beheld him striuynge in great agonye with the eye of faith, and
to rejoice with those that rejoiced, weep with those that weep, outwardly
having strife, and fear inwardly, desiringe to be dissolved and to be with
Christ.

Mat. 11.
Our LORD says of him self, learn of me, for I am meke and lowly of heart.

Our Lord took patiently the injuries that were done unto him by word and deed.
By backbitigne words, contradictorius, tauntinge and contumelious words.
They slaundred him both priuelye and openly, pryuelye within them selves, and
judging him temerariously and falsely, if this manne were a Prophet, he would

All hayle king of Jews. And with deed, when they crownde him with thorn,

We must think and ^ounder the diverse s^ourginges of our lord. Mar. 15.
For first he was scourged upon the head, he was smitten upon the head with a

And upon the face. One of the ministers which slode by the bishop, smote him

And to the heap of all iniuryes, it makes, that the lord of all lords and

The Jews ministers, says John, took Jesus, and bound him.

Also he was less esteemed the^ a thief for the Jews demanded yt Barrabas

And Jesus in the mids.

Forthermore we must way and ponder, that he was afflicted and punyshed in all
the members and senses of his body. His eyes beheld and saw those cruel
tormentors. And also his most mekest mother the which in soul was
crucified, and his derely beloved disciple, and the devout women that in mind
suffered with him. His ears did hear blasphemouse, mocking, injurious, and
dispising words. Likewise his nose, by reason of the place in the which he
was crucified, where the misdoers were beheaded, might with filthy slenche be
offended. His taste was noied because they gave him wine mingled with myrre, or
vinegar with gall to quench his thurst withal, whereby we may well understand,
that the drink which they gave him was very bitter. His sense of feeling or
touching sprede thorowout all his body, felt pain in his members which were
scourged, and in his hands and feet. Which were board through with nails.

It may be likewise considered, John. 19.
that he sustained loss in things longing and pertaining to his body. For he
was spoiled of his raiment: and his friends went from him. Mar. 14.
For his disciples for soke him, and ran away. Thus he was afflicted, as it is
said in all parts of his body, by his most bitter passion:

Also in heart and mind he suffered, for he was sorye for his friends that
stood by: and for his enemies that ignorauntly did crucify him.

And again in a manner he sufferd and was hurt in his good name and fame. Mat.
27.
For they called him a seductor of the people. Sir said the chief of ye
priests to Pilate, we remember yt this deceiuer said while he was yet a live.
etc.

And yet we must mark as touching the helthfull passion of our Lord Jesus
Christ, that it was most fylthy and most ignominius and shameful, be reason of
ye place, because it was done in Jerusalem. Where he was known and honored, and
where he had done many miracles. Item because of the time and day, for it was
done in the solemn feast of Ester, when a great multitude came together unto
the feast, and he was led unto his cross and passion at nine of the clock, to
then^ent he might be seen and known of all men. And again it was most
fylthy considering the kind of death. For it was the death of the cross, a
death dew unto ill spoken men, ill doers, and unjust men. And the manner
of going to his death. Jesus went forth bearing his cross the which
thing is not red of other two wicked persons which were led with him. John. 19.
And again by reason of his companions. For he was crucyfied betwixt ii.
thieves, asthough he had been one of the^, or the greatest or master of them.

Forthermore the bitterness of his blessed passyo^ was increased by ye natural
complexion of our lords body. For manifest it is yt his holy bodi was of ye
best and most purest co^plectio^: made and fashioned by the work of the holy
ghost, without any fault or error of nature, and so his holy flesh had no
rebellion or fight against the spirit: And therefore the spirit did love, and
not without a good cause, his body, more then any other man's spirit or soul
should love his body. Item the bitterness of his passion was agrauate by ye
continuance of the same. For many mar^irs that were burnt, or drowned, or
beheaded, did accomplish and end their martyrdom very shortly. But our
Lords passion endured even in a manner from thinstance of his conception,
until the hour of his death. For he foreknewe most certenlye, what his
humanity should suffer: but specially it continued from the time of his last
supper, until the nynthe hour of the syxte day following, And also it was
aggrauate by the quality of the members, in the which he suffered, that is, in
his fete and hands, ye which are members full of neaues and sinews, and most
ready to receive dolor and pain. And that our lords passyo^ was most bitter,
and very grievous, it may be most chefely gathered by this yt Luke shows, for
in his oration and prayer had after supper, his sweat through the vehement
imaginacion of the anguishe and pains that were to come, Luc. 22.
were like drops of blood, trickeling down to the ground.

But that our Lord went freely and willingli unto his passion, that made it most
gracious: Mat. 26.
R^^e, says he, let us be going. Behold, he is at hand that shall betray me.
And Ihon says, he went forth to mete the ministers that sought Jesus of
Nazareth, John. 18.
and when they hard our Lord say, I am he, they went backewardes, and fell to
the ground.

And when he was taken, bound, ignominious^y led away, falsely accused,
buffeted, be spued, scourged, mockingly crowned with thorn, yet he never
showed any word or sign of impacience or trouble: but showed them manifold
benefits that so did handle him. For he healed the servant ear that was
cut of, he spoke many devout and profitable words unto the^, and praid meekely
for those that crucified him, calliuge most swetely upon his father,
beninglye excusinge them, Luc. 23.
saying father. Forgive them, for they wotte not what they do.

And all this he suffered not for him self, but for us. For he prayed that the
sins might be taken away, which he never committed. And so he dyed for our
necessity and vtilitye, and not for his own, but for all his friends. For why,
to deliver us, he would be taken, to redeem us, he would be sold, that we might
be honored, he would be confounded and crucified. He was bound, that we might
be losed, scourged, that we should not be scourged, he died, that we should
not die eternally. And Paul says, I live by the faith of the son of God,
which loved me, and gave him self for me. And in a another place. Christ died
for our sins. Gala. 2.
And Peter says, Christ suffered for us, 1. Cor. 15.
leaninge us an ensample that we should follow his steps. 1. Pet. 2.
And Esaias, Esai. 33.
he was wounded for our offenses, and was smitten for our wickedness, and
with his stripes, we are healed. And it is written, I give my life for my sheep.

Of abstinence and sobriety. Capi. lxxxvii.
OUr lord commanded Adam saying. Genesis 2.
Eat thou of all the trees of paradyse, but as touching the tree of knowledge
of good and evil you shall not eat of it. In the which prohibition abstinence
is commended, in yt he would not ye man in paradise should eat of all manner of
meat.

Moses was in ye mount with our lord.40. days and 40 nights, Exo. 24.
and he nether did eat nor drink. Abstinence is a right good dysposition to
receive divine revelations: And manne refreshed with divine revelations, is
wont to abhor bodily delight and pleasure. Yea, Leuiti. 15
and our Lord commanded the children of Israel to abstain from diverse meats.

When either man or woman did vow a vow to be sanctified, Nume. 6.
or did consecrate or appoint the^ selves unto our lord, they abstained from
all such kinds of drink, as might cast them into dronckennesse.

The Aungel appearinge unto ma^nas wife which should conceive him, Iudi. 13.
that should deliver the people, commanded her to abstain.

This makes much to the commendation of sobriety, ye which does stand in the
use of fish, and in ye abstinence from flesh: that our lord in his gospel does
even often times multiply fish, Luke. 5.
and not flesh. And at our lords commandment the disciples in closed a
great multitude of fishes, Mark. 6.
furthermore we read yt he twyse multiplied bread and fishes. Luke. 9.
And of.v. loves, Ihon. 6.
and ii. fishes in Marcke. Math. 15.
Luke, and John And of.7. loves and a few fishes ye which our lord multiplied,
Mark. 8.
mention is made i^ Mat and Mark.

Peter purposinge to show that the disciples, Acts. ^.
which were replenished with the holy ghost, were not drunken, said that it was
not yet the third hour of the day. Geuynge us to wit, that it was not
convenient to drink before the third hour.

Of matrimony. Capitu. lxxxix.
IT is evident that a wife ought to be in many things unto her husband a
fellow and equale, Genesis 2.
but not a mistress nor a maid, because that our lord made her of Adams ryb,
and not of his head, nor of his foot. Again it is manifest, that manne is
the head of the woman, for as much as he is in a manner the beginning of her
being: and the woman was made of the man, not the man of the woman. And
therefore the man must be the master and the instructor: And the co^mmaundement
was given unto Adam by God, and by Adam to Eve.

Because ye one man ought to have but one wife, Genesis 2.
therefore our lord says: They shall become one flesh.

It is red, Genesis 4.
that only Lamech before the flud had two wives.

Our Lord commanded that in Noah's Ark should be reserved so many males as
females: Genesis 7.
that there might be one for one.

as he believed that she had an husband.

Of Chastity. Cap. lxxxx.
AS long as our first parents were in Paradise, so long they were virgins, Genesis
4.
but after that they were cast out, it is written. That Adam knew Eve his wife.

When Sichem had defiled Dina Jacobs daughter, her brethren were very angry,
because he had wrought folly in Israel, Genesis 34.
in that he had lain with Jacobs daughter, which thing ought not to be done.
At length they slew him that had defiled her, and his father, and all the
people. And note, that that thing was done under the law of nature, and
before the law written. How much more then ought virginitye to be honored
under the law of grace, and fornicatyon punished?

Although Joseph was a servant that was bought, Genesis 39.
and a beutifull young man, without a wife, and provoked by his mistres, yet he
refused aduoutery, and had rather to offend her, and to be cast into prison,
then to lose his chastity.

Judas being unchaste, Genesis 38.
detested and abhorde the fornication of Thamar.

Dani. 13.

Of Humility. Capi. xcvii.
THe angel said unto Agar, turn again to thy mastresse, Genesis 16.

and governance of the people, Genesis 3.4.
the which our Lord put and appointed unto him, nor would not agree unto it,

And our Lord was angrye with Moses.

Moses despised not the profitable counsel of a heathen, Exo. 18.
but most humbly granted and agreed unto it.

The humility of Ihon the Baptist does diversely apear. John. 2.
For he did judge but meanly of him self, when that ye people perchance
esteemed him to be Christ. I am not Christ. Also he spoke lowly. John. 1.
I am a voice crying in the desarte. He denied him self to be Christ or a

He was in the desert.

and hard the word of God.

Peter answered our Lord most humbly, John. 21.

We may, and ought to take ye most notable examples of humility of our savior.
John. 7.
For he would be conceived in a despised country, that is in Galile. Of the
which it is written. Search and look, for out of Galile aryseth no prophet.
And Nathanaell wondering said. Can there come any good thing out of Nazareth?
John. 1.
Item he was borne, of an humble and a meke mother, the which said, Luc. 1.
Luc. 2.
he beheld the humility of his hand maiden. And in a small cotage, and a low
place, for she laid him in a maunger. And for the space of xxx. year, he was
in the world in a manner as unknown, so that there is nothing red of his
doings, but that he, when he was xii. year of age, Luc. 2.
remained at Jerusalem, and was found in the temple hearing, and questionyng,
and determinyng. The which thing makes against those presumptuous persons,
Luc. ii.
that take upon them to hastily the office of a teacher. And then he went down
with Mary and Joseph, and was obediente and subject unto them. Then being about
a xxx. year of age, he came to Ihon Baptist, to be baptized of him. But he sent
not for him. The which thing makes sore against those, mat. 3.
that disdain to go to their inferiors. Likewise he chose him lowly and pore
disciples, and wtal humility was conuersa^t among them, and taught them to be
meek humble, mat. 11.
saying: learn of me, for I am and mecke and lowly. And he called him self more
often the son of man, than ye son of god, although they were both two after the
two natures which were in him. Yet most commenly he would name him self after
thinferiour and lowest nature. He was conversant with men, Ihon. 2.
and would be present at pore marriages where they lacked wine. He went to no
costly and rich mariges, in the which there is most commonly enorme and
great excess. And when he knew, that they would come and take him up to make
him a king, John. 6.
he fled up into a mountain: Mat. 17.
and he paid as a servant or as an aliene the tribute monye. Luc. 9.
Nor he had not whereon to lay his head. And going about to castles and
villages, he went continually a foot, so that he being weary of his iourny,
John. 4.
set on the well, and desired the woman of Canane to give him drink. And when
he came to Jerusalem, he had no horse to ride upon, but an ass. And departing
from this world unto his father, mat. 21.
he left a special example of humilitye, when he washed his disciples fete,
and wyped them with the towel, Ihon. 13.
wherwyth he was girded. But in his passion, he most chefely humbled him self,
even to death, Philip. 2.
and not to all kinds of death, but to the death of the Cross, the which
kind of death was most shamefulst, as it appears in all the Gospelles. Of
this it may be noted, that proud men, and such as love the world, are wont to
be occupied about vii. things, and to desire the same, or specially to glory
in things obtained: the which things Christ hanginge on the cross lacked,
and had the contrary. They may be called these earthly abundance. Worldly
wisdom. Carnal pleasure. The fame and praise of the people. A rought of
servants. The fall of their enemies. A number of friends. But our Lord
Christ Jesus upon the Cross was most poorest, Ihon. 19.
for he was spoiled of his garments.

He was taken for a fool and unwise. For the preachinge of the cross, is to
them that pearish folishnesse. 1. Cor. 1.
Item he was di^famed, and called a deceauer of the people. For the hye
Pryestes said by him, we remember, that this deceiuer said, etc. And being upon
the cross he was well nie ouercummed, and inclinynge of his head gave up the
ghost. And there he had no friends. I have trodden the press my self alone, Esa.
63.
and of al people there is not one with me. My lovers and friends have thou put
away fro me. Psalm. 87.
And on the cross, he lacked servants, his Dyscyples left him, Psalm. 87.
and went from him. And I am made as a man without help.

When Peter came into Cesaria, Cornelius met him, and fell down, and worshypped

And in an another place he says. These hands have mynystred unto my

and to them that were with me.

He desired very diligently the prayers of other men, Roma. 15.

And Paul does inwardlye with his own words declare true humilitye, when he

which am not worthy to be called an Apostle. These. 3.
And again he says: 1. Cor. 15.
Jesus came into the world to save sinners, 1. Timo. 1.

but make your selves equal to them of the lower sort. And again, in meekness
of mind, Philip. 2.
let every man esteem another better then him self.

seat, and made an oration unto the people. Act. 12.
And the people gave a shoute, saying. It is the voice o^ a god, and not of man. And immedyately the Angel of our Lord smote him, because he gave
not God the honor. And he was eaten of worms, and gave up the ghost.

Sampson with his bare hands tare a Lion, Iud. 14.
neither told his father nor his mother what he had done.

Goliath the Philistine defied the hooste of the Israelytes, 1. regu. 17.
and demanded that one should come to fight with him hand to hand.

Adonias the son of Hagith exalted him self, saying, I will be king. 3.

But his kyngedome dured not long.

Benadab the king of Siria sent messengers unto the king of Israel, 3. regu.
20.
and said. Thus and thus do the gods to me. If the duste of Samaria be
ynnoughe for all the people that follow me. To take every man an handful. But

self, as he does that puts it of.

4. regu. 18
Rapsaces spoke hye and proud words in ye king of Assirians name, saying,

Iudi. 6.
Holofernes said to Achior, when we slaye them all as one man, then shalt thou

Aman being immitted and calde to Esthers banquet, sent for his friends and his
wife, Esther. 5.
and told them of the glory of his richesse, and of the multitude of his
children, and that he and the king only should dine with ye Queen. And yet
