prepared for Mardocheus.

Esaias has dysclosed the words of the king of ye Assirians: Esa. 10.
Thus have I done through ye power of mine own hand, and through my wisdom I
understood it. And there was no man yt durst move a feather, or open his
mouth, or once whysper.

This saying of the prophet, Esa. 14.
I will clyme up into heaven, and set my seat above the stars of God, and will
be like the highest of al, is literally understood and meant by Nabucho. etc.

Jeremy says of Moab. I know her stoutnesse, Iere. 48.
her boasting, her arrogance, and the pride of her stomach, and that virtue is
not by her.

Nabuchodonozor said unto Danyels three fellows, Dani. 3.
that would not worship his golden Image. What God is there, that may deliver
you out of my hands?

Nabuchodonozor walkyng in his haule, Dani. 4.
said: Is not this the great city of Babylon, which I my self have made a
kings court, with my power and strength for the honor of my majesty? while
these words were yet in his mouth, there fell a voice from heaven. etc.

When Sereon hard say, yt Judas had gathered unto him ye congregation of the
faithful, he said. I will get me a name, 1. Mac. 3
and overcome Judas, the which contrariwise, did overcome him sone after.

Demetrius the son of Demetrius sent unto Ionathas, saying: come down to us
into the plain field, ^. Match. x.
and there let us prove our strength together, thou shall find that I have
valiant men of war with me, ask and know whom I am. And yet his chance was
but evil.

Nicanor purposing to fight against the Jews, 2. Match. 8.
called merchant men unto him, promising that he would give them lxx. Jews for
one talent.

The multitude of armed men coming together, 2. match. 9.
Antiochus was put to flighte from Persepolis a city of Persia with shame and
dyshonoure. And yet he spoke proudly, saying, yt he would come to Jerusalem, and
make it a grave for the Jews.

Nicanor did ask of the Jews, whether there were a mighty one in heaven, 2.
match. 15
that commanded the Sabothe day to be kept. And when they said, the mighty
Lord in heaven commanded the seventh day to be kept, he said. And I am mighty
upon earth.

Peter said very boldlye unto our Lord. mat. 26.
Though all men be offended because of thee, yet will not I be offended. And
yet afterward it chanced far otherwise.

They that boast and crake most of them selves, Mat. 4.
do chance to lie, they follow specially the devil, the which when he had
showed our Lord all the kingdoms of the world, said: al these things are
delivered unto me, Luc. 4
and I give them to whom I will.

Our Lord against those that be bosters and arrogante, Luc. xviii
does bring in the example of that Pharisey, saying. I am not as other men
are, or as this Publicane.

The Phariseis spoke words of great arrogancye to him that was borne blind,
John. 9
and restored again to his sight by our Lord, and he with good reason
confounded them. Thou art all together borne in sin, and do thou teach us?

Pilate but to arrogantly said unto our Lord: John. 19
know thou not that I have power to crucify thee, and have power to lose
thee?

Of elections. Capitu. C.
MOses using Ietros the priest of Madians counsel, Exo. 18.
did elect and choose under judges or prelates men of actiuity and power, and
such as feared God, true men, and hatyng covetousness.

Our Lord commanded Moses to take xii. rods after the number of the tribes of
Israel, Nume. 17.
and the name of Aaron was in the tribe of Leui. And when he had put the^ in
the tabernacle, on ye morrow he found Aarons rod budded.

Moses purposing to revenge Israel of the Madianites, Nume. 31.
said. Let there be chosen a M. out of every tribe of Israel, to the wars.

When Moses which had disobeied the will of God, Nume. 27.
should die, he praid our Lord devoutly, saying. Let the Lord of the sprites of
all flesh, set a man over the congregation, and our Lord ordained that Iosue
the son of Nun should be his successor, and guide of the people in his stead.

After the death of Iosue, the children of Israel asked counsel of our Lord,
saying: Judith. 1.
who shall go up before us, and be the captain of the war? And our Lord said,
Judas shall go up.

When the men of Israel saw that Gedeon had fought strongly and ma^fully for
them: Iudi. 8.
they said al unto him, reign thou over us.

The elders of Galaad went unto Iepthe, Iud. 11.
and said unto him, come and be our prince and captain, and fight against the
children of Amnon.

There was a man of Benjamin named Eis, 1. regu. 9.10
the same had a son called Saul; a chosen and a good man, nor there was not
a better in all Israel. Our Lord disclosed unto Samuel that he should be
chosen, and anointed upon the people of Israel.

Samuel at the special commandment of our Lord went to Bethleem, 1. regu. 16.
and anointed David the son of Isai king upon Jerusalem and Israel.

Saul being dead, the men of the tribe of Judah came and anointed David king
over the house of Judah: 2. regu. 2.
after that, 2. regu. 5.
all the tribes of Israel came unto him, and anointed him king over all the
people of Israel. And therefore he says in his Psalms, he has chosen his
servant David. And in a another place. 1. Para. 28.
It has pleased our Lord, to choose me king over all the people of Israel.

And David drawing toward his death, 1. Para. 28.
said unto the elders of Israel. Of all my sons, our Lord has chosen
Solomon my son to sit upon the seat of the kingdom of our Lord in Israel.

Jeroboam by the terrible judgment of God was chosen and taken to be king over
ten tribes of Israel. 3. regu. 12.
And yet he was the occasion that the people departed and went from god.

Iehu wrote letters, and sent to Samaria unto the rulers and best of the city.
4. regu. 10.
Of all our masters sons choose the best, and him that shall please you, and
set him on his fathers seat, and fight for your Lords house.

All Judas friends came together, and said unto Ionathas, 1. match. 9.
for so much as thy brother Judas is dead, there is none like him to go forth
against our enemies. Wherefore we this day chose thee for him, to be our
Prince and captain to order and to fight our battle.

Our Lord called his disciples, and of them he chose twelve, Luc. 6.
whom he called apostles.

After the assention of our Lord, the disciples appointed two, Joseph and
Mathias: Act. 1.
and when they prayed, they said. Thou Lord which know the hearts of all
men, show whether of those two thou have chosen to take the ministration of
this apostleshyp upon him.

The sayings of the apostles pleased the whole multitude. Act. 6.
And they chose Steven a man full of faith, and full of the holy ghost, and
Philippe etc.

As the Discyples minystred to our Lord and fasted, the holy ghost said.
Separate me Barnabas and Saul, Act. 13.
for the work where unto I have called them.

Of good Princes and Prelates. Ca. Ci.
MOses the good prelate went in oftentimes to Pharao, to deliver the people
from the Egipeiacal servitude and bondage. Ex. 67.8.9


Moses did comfort the people that were afraid, saying. Fear ye not, stand still,
Exo. 14.
our Lord shall fight for us, and ye shall hold your peace. He spoke with his
mouth, but praid our Lord with his heart, as it appears there.

Exo. 15
Moses cried for the people unto our lord, when they murmured against him.

A good prelate must refer all things to our Lord. Exo. 16
And so Moses said, your murmuringes is not against us, but against our lord.

Moses when Israel fought against Amelech, went not to the battle, but sent
his servant Iosue only, and yet as touching his part, the war was just. Exo.
17.
But he standinge in the top of the hill, applied and turned him to prai unto
our lord.

When Moses should depart from the people, Exo. 23
and ascend up to the mountain, he left them two good vicares and gouernoures,
that is Aaron and Hur.

Our lord seemed to be willing to confound and destroy the sinful people,
Exo. 32
and promised unto Moses great dignity and honor. And yet Moses did pray
instantly for the people, And note, with what seueritye he punyshed the people,
for whom he prayed our Lord so instantly.

Moses gave unto the Levites xii. oxen, and vii. charettes, Numer. 7.
the which the lords of the tribes of Israel had offered. But he gave nothing
to the children of Caath, although they were nearer of kin unto him, because
their office was to hear all things upon their shoulders.

Moses wished and desired that all the Lords people could Prophecye.
Notwithstanding that his honor, as it seemed, Nume. 11.
should thereby have been deminished.

After that the spies were returned, our Lord said to Moses, Nume. 14
how long do this people provoke me, and how long will it be or they believe
me? I will smite them therefore with the pestylence, and will make of the a
prince of a greater nation, and mightyer then this is. But Moses would be
preserde no hier.

The people pearishing for the tumult and murmuringe that they made against
Moses and Aaron, Nume. 16.
Moses said to Aaron. Take a censare, and put fire therein out of the aultare,
and pour on cense. and go quicklye unto the congregation, that thou may
pray and obtain the forgeneuesse for them.

When Moses should dye, Nume. 27.
he prayed our Lord most diligently that he would provide the people of a
meet and a good captain. But yet in special he would name none.

Israel served our Lord all the days of Iosue. etc. Iosu. 24.
For why a good prelate is very mete to direct the people in the way of our
Lord.

Samuel judged al Israel and went about Bethel. Calgala, 1. regu. 7.
and Masphat, that they which had need of him, might the easlyer come unto
him.

Samuel said unto the people. God keep me from this sin, 1. regu. 12.
yt I should cease to pray for you, and I will teach you a right way and a
good.

When David saw the Angel yt smote the people, 2. regu. 24.
he offered him self to be beat for them, let thine hand (I pray the) turn
against me.

Al they of Israel hard of the judgment, which the king had judged between
the two women, 3. regu. 3.
and they feared the king, for they saw that the wisdom of God was in him to
do justice.

It is a sign and a token that our Lord does love the people when he gives
them a good prelate. 3. regu. 9.
For the Queen of Saba said, our Lord loved Israel, and therefore he made ye
king over it, to do equity and righteousness.

3. regu. 20.
Our Lord being purposed and wyllinge to deliver the king of Siria into the
king of Isreal's hands, sent him word by his prophet, that the king should
begin to fight and give battle.

As long as Ioiada the bishop lived, 4. regu. 12.
Ioas the king of Judah was good, and did that which was good in the sight of
our Lord. But the bishop being dead, he did much harm.

Iosaphat the king of Judah, set judges in the land over the people, and did
faithfullye, 2. Para. 19.
and wisely instruct them. Take heed, says he, what ye do, for ye execute not
the judgment of man, but of God, which is with you in the judgment.
Wherefore now, let the fear of God be upon you, and take heed, and be doing
the thing that pleases him, for there is no unrighteousness with the Lord
our GOD, that he should have any respect of persons, or take rewards.

Hezechias king of Judah caused the brazen serpent to be broken in pieces: 4.
regu. 18.
because it was unto the people an occasion of committinge ydolatry.

The posts went with letters thorowoute all Israel and Judah at the kings
commandment and his Lords, 2. Para. 30.
saying. Turn again unto our Lord. etc.

As Esdras was prayinge and weeping for the transgression of the people, 1. Esd.
9.
there resorted unto him a great company of men and women, and the people
folowinge his ensample wept and lamented very sore.

Eliachim the hye preast hearing of the power of Holofernes, Judith. 4.
went round about all Israel: and spoke unto them saying. Be ye sure, that
our Lord will hear your petitions, if ye continue steadfast in fasstinges
and prayers in the syghte of our LORD. And thus he comforted the people with
good exhortations.

A good prelate must be as a good father unto ye people committed unto him For
it is written by Esai of Eliachim, whom our lord set and did constitute in
Sobnas the rulers place: Esa. 22.
he shall be as a father of such as dwell in Jerusalem.

After that Judas Machabeus was dead, 1. match. 9.
there spronge up wicked persons throughout all costs of Israel, and exhorted
all such as did evil, to wickedness. And in those days there was great
hunger. etc.

When men thought that Ionathas was slain by Tryphon. 1. Match. 12.
Then all the heathen that were round about them, sought to destroy them.
For they said, now have they no captain, nor any man to help them. Therefore
now let us overcome them, and rote out their name from among men.

It is well said, that the prudencye and pitye of Onias the hye preaste, 1.
Match. 3.
and the goodness of other godly subjects, was the cause of peace, and good
estate of the holy city.

Onias did well resyste Heliodorus, going about to spoil the temple, 2. mac.
3.
and to take away such things as was laid up for wyddowes and fatherless
children.

Our savior and lord Jesus, where he calls him self a good shepherde, John.
10.
by and by he submits the cause, saying, a good shepharde gives his life
for the sheep. And again I give my life for the sheep. Whereby he does us to
understand, what thing is required, that a man may be called a good
shephearde.

When our Savior, after his resurrection, was minded to commit the
congregation of the church to Peter: first he proved him, John. 22.
saying, Simo^, love thou me more then these? And note, that he examined him
of dilection, and not of knowledge, not of practice, or contemplation, but of
the deed, not of the law. Nor he asked him not once, but thryee. If thou love
me, feed my sheep, clyppe them not, nor slaye them. For why a good prelate
must feed his sheep, with word, example, and bodily food.

Peter perceyuinge that the Jews marueled, and judged evil of the discyples,
lifted up his voice, and said unto them. Act. 1.
Ye men of Iewrye. etc. where he defends his flock most constantly, and
most holsomlye overcomes his adversaries.

We may consider here by Paul, the prelate of all excellent goodness, that
dilection does most specyallye pertain to a good prelate. John. 10.
For the prince and chefest of all pastoures did so love his sheape, that he
gave his life for his sheape. The which loved them even to the latter end.
And Paul was marvelous feruente in that kind of dilectyon and love. And
therefore he said. I will very gladlye bestow, and will be bestowed for your
souls, 2. Cor. 12.
though the more I love you, the less I am loved again.

Item there ought to be in a prelate the science and knowledge of scripture.
Choose and love the light of wisdom, Sapi. 6.
the which does profyt the people. Or elsse how can he dyscerne Leprosy, 1.
Cor. ^.3.
from no Leprosye, or judge the people committed unto him. Paul had an
excellent knowledge both in divine and humain matters, he gave unto babes in
Christ milk to drink, and spoke wisdom among those that are perfect. And he
was taken up into the third heaven, 2 Cor. 12.
and hard secreat words which no man can utter.

The love of subjects, and knowledge of scriptures, causes a presydent or a
prelate to be dilygent. Roma. 12.
Let him, says Paul that rules, do it with diligence. The which
solicitude and diligence Paul used most fervently toward his neighbors.
And therefore he says, beside the things which outwardlye happen unto me, I
am combred dailye, and do care for all Congregatyons. 2. Cor. 11.
And in a another place. I would ye knew how great solicitude and care that I
have for you. Collo. 2.
Of and by these three foresaid things thinstruction of the learned does
follow, and therefore our Lord does promise by Jeremy: saying, I will give
you herdmen after mine own mind, which shall ^eade you with learning and
wisdom.

As Artaxerzes said to Esdras, and to the judges of the people. 1. Esd. 7.
Teach the unlearned frelye, the which thing Paul the doctor of the heathen
has done evidently, teaching the universal world other by word or writing a
teacher of the gentiles with faith and verity and opens the savor of his
knowledge by us in every place. i. Timo. 2.
2 Cor. 2.


Also a good prelate ought to dispose and orden his offices among his
subjects, Exo. 18.
as Moses did, the which by the counsel of Iethro made among the people
rulers over hundreds, over fifty, and over ten. Paul did the like in ye church.
i. Cor. 11
Other things will I set in order when I come. And for yt thing he said unto
Tite. For this cause left I thee in Creta, that thou should reform the
things that are imperfect, Tite. i.
and should ordain elders and priests in every city, as I had appointed
thee.

Item a good Prelate must animate and comfort the weaklings and fearful, exo.
14.
as Moses did, when he said unto the fearful people, fear not, our lord shall
fight for you. And Paul did that thing very well, saying. Be strong and of
good comfort in our Lord, Ephe. 6.
and through the virtue and power of his might, put on all the armor of god.
etc. And again. Consider how that he endured such speaking against him of
sinners, Heb. 12.
least ye should be wearyed and faint in your minds.

A good Prelate should defend the oppressed: as Onias the hie priest did, the
which did constantly resist Heliodorus going about to spoil the temple, 2.
match. 3
and how valiantly Paul wythstode the false Prophets, 2. Cor. 11.
it is manifest in the Acts. And he says, where in so ever any man dare be
hold, I dare be bold also. And therefore he said yt he fought. So fight I. not
as one that beats the air. And I have fought a good fight. 2. Timo. 4.
I have fulfilled my course.

A good Prelate should be a comforter of thafflicted, as Eliachim did, when
Holofernes besieged Bethelia. And Paul was equal with him in this part, and
says. Blessed be God the father of our Lord Jesus Christ, which is the
father of mercy, and the God of all comfort, 2. Cor. 1.
which comfort us in all our tribulation, in so much that we are able to
comfort them, which are in any manner of trouble. And again. I beseech you
brethren, suffer the word of consolation or exhortation. Heb. 13.
And such words of consolation he used specially to the Philippians and
Thessalonia^s, as it is manifest to those that will search and look for it.

It good prelate must stir up those that be flouthful and cold. Genesis 42
As Jacob the Patriarch did, the which hearing that there was vitailes and
corn to be sold in Egypt, said to his children. Why do you neglecte it? And
that thing could that noble Paul do full well. It is now time (says Paul)
that we should awake out of sleep. And he says: Awake thou that sleapest,
and stand up from death, Roma. 13.
and Christ shall give thee light. And again. Ephe. 5.
I warn thee that thou stir up the gift of GOD which is in thee, by the
putting on of my hands.

A good prelate in as much as he may, 2. Timo. 1.
must help the neady to have that that is necessary for them. We have an
ensample of that in Elizeus, the which did distribute to the children of the
prophets twentye loves. 4. regu. 4
The which thing Paul did fulfill most diligently, having in remembrance
these words. It is more blessed to give, Act. 20.
then to receive, as he says. And when he had not what to give, he procured
it of other me^, as it does well apeare to the Corinthians. 1. Cor. 16.
Concerning the gathering. etc. and again. He which sows little, 2. Cor. 9.
shall reap little.

It pertains to a good prelate to bring those low that are proud. And
Moses purposing to do the same said rebukyngly. Nume. 16.
Ye make much to do, ye children of Leuy. And Samuel said unto Saul.
Wherefore have thou not harkened unto the voice of our Lord.

And Paul was very well learned in this art, saying. Some swel as though I
would come no more to you, i. regu. 15.
but I will come to you shortly, if God will, and will know not the words of them
which swell, 1. Cor. 4.
but the power. And in another place. Charge them which are rich in this
world, that they be not proud and hie mineded. 1. Timo. 6.


Again a good Prelate ought personally to viset those which are far of, i.
regum. 7
and are not able to come unto him the which thing Samuel did fulfill. For he
went about Bethel, Calgala, and Masphat, and judged the people. And who at any
time exercysed that thing as Paul did? the which from Jerusalem to the latter
sea, Roma. 15.
filled all places with the Gospel of Christ, and so, that he named his life a
certain course. i. Cor. 9.
I therefore so run, not as at an uncertain thing. 2. Timo. 4.
And I have fulfilled my course.

Also a good Prelate ought to punish transgressors, exo. 31.
as Moses did, when they worshipped and prayed unto the molten calfe. Nor Paul
was not neglygente in this part, but said. The weapons of our warfare are
not carnal things, 2. Cor. 10.
but things mighty in God. Then there follows. And are ready to take
vengaunce on all dysobedyence. And also. i. Cor. 4.
Shall I come unto you with a rod, or elsse in love, and in the spryte of
softness?

A good Prelate ought to extirpe and wede out the stubburne and pestyferous
from among the people: as Moses did with Chore and his, which claue unto him.
Nume. 16.
Separate says he, and stand thou and all the congregation alofe. And then
unto the other he said. Depart from the tents of these wicked men. And Paul
says of him that kept his mother in law. I have determined to deliver him
unto Satan for the destruction of the flesh. 1. Cor. 5.
And afterward. Pourge ye the old leven. And he delivered unto Satan
Hymeneus and Alexander, 1. Timo. 1.
to learn not to blaspheme.

And to make an end, this good prelate must pray for all men, Exodi. 32.
as Moses did, the which prayed unto our lord. And as Samuel did. God forbid
that I should sin against our Lord, 1. regu. 12.
and cease praying for you. And Paul did fulfill this thing most diligently,
Roma. 1.
without ceasing I make mention of you in my prayers. And again. We pray
always for you that our God will make you worthy of his calling, 2. These. 1.
etc. And he exhorted that it might be done. I pray you that above all
things, prayers may be had for all men, i. Timo. 2.
and kings.

Of evil princes and prelates. Capi. Cii.
OUr Lord commanded Moses saying: Nume. 15
Take all the heads of the people, and hang them up before the Lord against
the son:

Moses said unto Aaron, what did this people unto thee, Exodi. 32.
that thou haste brought so great a sin upon them? as though he would say, ye
prelate should sin greatly against his subjects, that would incline to their
evil will and purposes.

Elye corrected his sons but slenderlye, the which thing dyspleased our
Lord very sore, 1. regu. 2.
and yet with words he corrected and reprehended them, but he did it but
softely. and not profitably nor sharply, what shall we then say of those that
favor men in mischefe, or of those that give men an occasion of evil?

The whole wayt of the battle turned upon Saul, and so he fell and was
slain. i. regu. 31.


For David's sin that he committed when he nu^bred his people, 2. reg. 24.
there dyed of the people seventy thousand men.

Because Roboam would ouerpresse and charge his people, 3. regu. 12.
he lost ye greatest part of them.

Jeroboam gave an occasion to the people to depart and leave God, 3. regum. 12.
when he made calves of gold, and commanded ye people to adore and worship
them.

Subjects by the occasion of evil prelates and rulers are at some times
temporallye punished. 3. regu. 18.
Whereupon Helias said to Achab. Thou troublest al Israel, and thy fathers
house.

The king of Siria commanded the captains of his Charettes, 3. reg. 22.
thus. Fight neither with small nor great, save only against the king of
Israel. And that was only against that most wicked Achab.

Manasses made Judah and the inhabiters of Jerusalem to err, 2. Para. 33.
and to do worse then the Heathen, whom our Lord destroyed before the children
of Israel.

Esaias has expressed the sins and fautes of the euel rulers and prelates that
dwelt in Jerusalem, esa. i.
saying: Thy princes are wicked and companyons of thieves. They love gifts all
together, and gape for rewards.

And of Nabuchodonozor a very euel prince and governor, esa. 14.
it is said. Thou have wasted thy land, and destroyed thy people.

Sobna the ruler of the temple believed that he should live long in Jerusalem,
and when he should dye, to be honorably buried. But our Lord said thus
unto him. What have you to do here, and whom have thou here? And a non after
there follows. I will drive the from thy station and dwelling place. Esa. 22.
And he seems to be of those, the which said a little before. Let us eat
and drink, for to morrow we shall dye.

Sedechias said unto his estates that desired the death of Jeremy. Iere. 38.
Lo, he is in your hands, for the king may deny you nothing.

Our Lord by his prophet Ezechiel speaks against evil prophets and
prelates. Ezechi. 13.
Ye ascended not against them, neither made you a wall for the house of
Israel, that ye may abide ye better in the day of our Lord.

Our lord most terribly does threaten evil and naughty prelates by his prophet
Ezechiell, saying, Woe be unto you shepheardes of Israel that feed your
selves, should not the shepheardes feed the flocks? By and by he discryueth
the deeds of ill pastors, Ye have eaten up the milk, Ezech. 34.
ye have clothed you with the woll, the best fed have ye slain. The sick have
ye not healed, the broken have ye not bound (...)

When the head preaste saw that the Apostles did many signs and wonders, Act.
5.
he rose up, and al they that were with him, and laid hands on the Apostles
and put them into the common prison. But the Aungel of our lord by night,
brought them forth. Then went the Magistrates with ministers and brought
them again. And after many and long counsels they calde the Apostles unto
them, beat them, and commanded that they should not speak in the name of
Jesus.

The Jews caughte Steven, and brought him to the counsel, and when the chief
preastes had objected and laid many things unto him, Act. 6.7.
then said they, is it even so? When he had truly and faithfully defended
him self, and sharply reproved them, they stoned him to death.

Certain men having a damsel, whom Paul delivered of a spryte which
Prophesied, Act. 16.
accused him in such wise and Silas his companion, that they troubled all the
city. The Magistrates and Judges with out any probation there of, commanded
the^ to be beaten, and to be thruste into the hard and inner prison.

When Paul was brought into the counsel he began to speak resonablye, but
even at the first word that Paul spoke, Act. 23.
the hye preaste commanded him to be smytten. Then said Paul. God shall smite
the thou painted wall. Syttest thou and iudgest me after the law, and
commaundest me to be smitten contrary to the law?

Paul had evil and wicked Judges, Felyx and Festus, Act. 25.
the which would please and gratify the Jews, and therefore Paul was
constrained to appeal.

MAry and Aaron spoke against Moses, Nume. 12.

Chore and his company desyringe to come to ye governance of the people,

seeing all the multitude is holy, and that our lord is among them. Why heue

Abimelech Gedeons son did craftily procure by his mothers friends that he

but yet afterward it chanced very vnluckely unto them both.

Ptolomy the son of Abobus had abundance of silver and gold, 1. Match. 16.

Of the deuels temptation. Ca. Ciiii.
THe serpent being crafty to te^pt ye the deuel in the serpent, approached the
feblest part of ma^kinde, and the most prompest to sin for he tempted not
Adam first, Gene. 3.
but Eve. And began searchynge a far of, for he counseld them not even suddenly
to eat of the forbidden fruit. And he denied that there should follow any
pain for the transgressyon of the commandment. Yea he affyrmde that great
goodness should follow that only eating of the apple.

The lying spirit does oftentimes lie in his temptation, Gene. 3.
for he said unto Eve, ye shall not dye the death. And he said unto our
Savior, when he showed him all the kingdoms of the world. Luc. 4.
They are delivered unto me, and to whom I will, I give the^. And furthermore
he alleges holy scripture peruersly and falsely: saying unto the LORD of
aungelles. He has given his angels charge over thee. Math. 4.


And Satan stood up against Israel, and provoked David to nombre Israel. 1.
Para. 21.


Satan required of our Lord, that Job might be touched in his goods, Job. 1.2.
children, and body. Wherein may be noted, the subtelty, malignity, and
infirmity of our ennemy.

It is not expedient to dysclose our temptations to any such man, whom we
believe to have been tempted with like sin. But rather to some dyscreat and
holy man, that would comfort us in goodness. Wherefore when the two old men,
did reuele and open their concupiscence one to a another, Dani. 23.
they were provoked to that, that was worse.

The Lords temptation does teach us to overcome al kinds of temptation. Luc.
4.
He was tempted in three things, unto the which, all other temptations may be
reduced. And note, that he overcame not temptation by power, but by scripture.

strength thy brethren.

Of sin in general, and of diverse pains which follow sin. Ca. Cv.
THat sin does cause shamfastnesse in man, it is evident, for when our first
parents in the state of innocencye were bare, Gene. 3.
they were not ashamed: but after they had trespassed, by and by they made them
selves aprons.

Sin does defame a sinner. And therefore Adam after that he had trespassed,
Gene. 3.
thought to have hid him self from the presence of our Lord. Sin likewise
makes a man fearful, for after ye Adam had sinned, Gene. 3.
he said, I was afraid, because I was naked, and hid my self.

The enormity of sin does cry to the ears of our Lord for ve^gance, Gene.
4.
As the voice of thy brothers blood. And in a another place. The cry of the
Sodomites. At some times our Lord does punyshe sin with temporal pain and
punyshmente. As it is euydent in Adam and Eve. Ge. 3.4.19
In Cain. In the Sodomytes. And often in the children of Israel. And Christ
said. Sin no more, Ihon. 5.
least a worse thing happen unto thee.

Pharao knowledged and confessed yt he was scourged and punished of our Lord for
sin, Exo. 10.
saying. I have sinned against our Lord and against you.

The children of Israel did evil in the sight of our Lord. And our Lord was
angry, Judith. 2.
and delivered them into the hands of raueners, that took and spoiled them,
and sold them into the hands of their enemies.

Of the wickedness of tirauntes. Ca. Cix.
PHarao invented diverse wyckednesses to extinguyshe, Exo. 1.
or to reduce the children of Israel to a smaller number. First of all, he
commanded to punysh them with hard labor. Secondarelye he commanded the
male children to be killed, but afterward he commanded that they should be
cast into the river and that the women children should be saved. First Pharao
said even simply, I know not the Lord, nether will I let Israel go. Exo. 5.
And again he granted it unto them saying, go ye, and do sacrifyce unto the
Lord in this land. And yet afterward he would let the^ go to do sacrifice
unto our Lord in the wilderness, so that they went not far of. Exo. 10.
And after that he was content that the men should go, so that they left
their shepe^ their cattle behind the^.

Paul departinge from Ephesus, and preachinge boldly the word of God, and

A certain manne named Demetrius a silver smyth, which made silver shrynes for

into the air: Act. 22.

When the hye captain had Paul in hold: mo then fortye Jews said unto the

Paul standinge before Felyx the Debity, the Jews accused him that he was a
pestilente fellow and a seditious, Ac. 24.25

Of the mobility, and inconstancy of the people. Ca. Cxiiii.
MOses returning out of the la^d of Madian into Egypt, told all the words of
our Lord, for the which he had sent him: Then follows. And the people
believed. And when they hard that our Lord had sanctified the children of
Israel, they bowed their head, and worshypped. But afterward when they were
afflicted by Pharaos task masters, Exo. 4.5
they said to Moses and Aaron. Our Lord look upon you and judge, which has
made the savor of us stink in the eyes of Pharao, and in the eyes of his
servants: and have put a swearde in their hand to slay us.

When that the children of Israel, after mani plages of Egypt, came out of
Egypt enriched and armed, our lord going before them, and showing them the
way by a cloud and fire, Exo. 14.15.
they saw the Egiptians following after them, and were sore afraid.

And said unto Moses: because there were no graves in Egypt, haste thou
therefore brought us away for to dye in the wilderness? After that they were
comforted by Moses, when our Lord divided the sea, that they passed over dry
foted, and that Pharaos host was drowned, then the people feared our Lord,
and believed him, and his servant Moses, saying: we will sing unto the Lord.

And sone after coming to Marath, the people murmured because the waters were
bitter: and when they were made sweet by castinge in of a little wodde, Exo.
15.16.
they murmured again for lack of meat, and said unto Moses and Aaron, would
to God we had dyed in the land of Egypt, when we sat by the flesh pots, and
our Lord at the even tide sent them quayles, and in the morning he sent
them Manna.

After this when he should give the^ the law: Exo. 19.
they said. All that our Lord has said, we will do.

And when Moses had showed them ye words and precepts, the which he had
received of our Lord, Exo. 24.
they said. All the words which our Lord has said, will we do.

But when Moses staid long in the mount with our Lord about the description of
the tabernacle, Exo. 32.
the people gathered them selves together unto Aaron, and said. Make us Gods to
go before us.

After that the Tabernacle was reared up, Nume. 11.
and that the chief men, after that the fighting men and Levites were

as greaued by much labor.

After that the people had hard the spies relation, they murmured and wept.

When that Paul, after the shypwracke that happened in the winter, was

No doubt this man is a murderer: whom though he have escaped the sea, yet

mynds, and said that he was a God.

Of good operations and works. Capitu. Cxv.
OUr Lord put man in the garden of pleasure, to dress and keep it. Genesis 2.3.

taken and made. And so note thou, that our LORD would manne to labor both
in the state of innocencye, and also after his fall.

was much greater, yet he accomplyshed all in a less time.

Of good prosperity. Capitu. Cxxi.
THe abundance of temporal things, is oftentimes the occasion of much
sin, as in that regyon and country the which was watered, and like the
garden of our Lord, Genesis 13.
and like the land of Egypt as thou co^mest unto zoar, the which the wicked
Sodomites did inhabit.

When Gedeon was little and threshed wheat, Iudi. 6.8.
he was good, and the Angel of our Lord did visit him. But after he had
obtained the victory against the Madianites, he mysbehaued him self.

Saul or ever he was made king, was good, 1. regu. 15.
but after he took upon him to rule, he waxed proud, and brake our Lords
commandment.

After that David had made great war and had gotten many victoies of his
ennemies, 2. regu. 11.
he remayninge in quietness at Jerusalem, committed aduouterye, and afterward
ensued murder.

David by the occasion of the multitude of his subjects, 2. regu. 24.
waxed proud: and caused his people to be numbered: But yet note, how grievously
he was punished.

In Salomons time silver was of no valor: 3. reg. 10.11
For in Jerusalem silver was as plenteous as stones. But note, how maruelus and
how terrible a thing it was that his abundaunce of things hurt him more,
then his wisdom auayled him,

Or ever Jeroboam had dominion and rule over the.x. tribes, 3 regu. 12.
we read not that he was evil, but that he was a good young man and a deligent:
but sone after he had obtained the kingdom, he made golden calves, and least
he should be turned out of his domynion and rule, he auerted and turned
the people from GOD.

Amasias the king of Judah made war against Edome. 4. reg. 14
Where upon his heart became proud, and intended to fight against Ioas the king
of Isell, but he prosperd not.

When Roboams kingedome was fortified, 2. Para. 11.
and comforted, he forsook the law of our Lord, and all Israel with him.

When Osias the king of Judah became mighty, 2. Para. 20.
his heart arose to his destruction for he went into the temple to burn
incense upon the altar of incense.

Manasses king of Jerusalem was exceadynge evil. 2. Para. 33
But afterward being bound in Babylon, and in tribulation, he prayde unto
our Lord, and did exceadinge great penance before our Lord.

They did eat and were filled, and became fat, 2. Esd. 9
and lived in wealth through thy great goodness. And provoked thee to anger.

Wordly prosperity does sometimes multiplye and much increase and bring
carnal friends together, Tobi. 2.11.
the which aduersitye does avoid and fly, for Tobias kinsmen and friends,
after he had recovered his sight, and was enriched, came unto him: the which
thing is not read that they did as long as he was blind, and that his wife
went to the weauinge work.

After that Nabuchodonozor had ouercomde Arphaxat the king of Medes, his
kingdom was exalted, Judith. 1.
and his heart was lift up.

Although Aman was next unto ye mighty and puissaunt king Ahaswerus, Esth. 3.5.
and had great richesse, children, and friends, yet he was troubled and vexed
that Mardocheus would not bow his kne unto him, as though he had had nothing.

Note the shortness of this prosperity. As long as the plage of the lord was
over Job, although certain friends came unto him, yet they were onerous and
heavy comfortors, nor it is not red that they gave him any thing. But after
the lord had given Job twice as much as he had before, then came there unto
him al his brethren, and all that had been of his acquaintance before, Job. 42.
and did comfort him: and every one gave him a sheep and an earing of gold.

The Image, which Nabuchodonozor saw, Dani. 2.
was smitten of a stone, hewn out of a mountain, and was broken to poulder,
does sufficientlye declare worldly prosperity to be nothing.

The Children of Zambry made a great marriage. 1. macha. 9.
And ye Jews with Ionathas slew many of them. Thus the marriage was turned
to mourning, and the noise of their melodye into lamentation.

The Jews received our Lord into Jerusalem solempnlye: math. 21.
but after he had well beheld them, toward even, he went to Bethany. For he

The example that our Lord does use, Luc. 12.
and put by the rich man, whose ground brought forth ple^tiful fruits, does
greatly serve us to despise the abundance of temporal things. For when he
most diligently thought to break down and destroy his barnes, and build
greater. God said unto him Thou fool, this night will the devils fetch away thy
soul from thee. Then whose shall those things be, which thou have provided?

The biers of the farm, and Oxen, and he that married a wife were calde to our
Lords supper, Luc. 14.
and they, as being busy about other things, excused them selves but the
poor, and the feeble were brought in.

Our Lord beholdinge the city of Jerusalem, Luc. 19.
being in temporal peace, and ignoraunte of the miseryes that were to come:
wept on it, saying. If thou had known, thou would weep.

When the people gave a shout, He rode having on his royal apparel, sitting
in his seat, and making an oration unto them, Act. 12.
they said. It is the voice of a God, and not of a man. And immediately the
angel of our lord smote him, because he gave not GOD the honor, and he was
eaten of Worms, and gave up the Ghost.

Of death in general. Cap. Cxxxi.
THe sentence of God wherewith he said unto man. Genesis 2.
In what dai so ever ye shall eat thereof, shall dye the death. It is plain
and evident that man as soon as sin is committed does die. So that the living
man, does die, as it were continuallye. As Saint Augustine says in his
fourtene book of the City of God.

Notwithstanding that men before the floude lived so many years, genesis 9.
yet scripture after the description of their lives, says. And he died.

It was no marvel that our fore fathers feared to die, and desired to be
long lived. For they as yet could not ascend up into heaven, nor have the
fruition of the divine vision, until the coming of our savior, the which
opened the gates of heaven. And therefore holy Lot was monyshed to save him
self in the mountain. Genesis 19.
He feared to go thither, least some misfortune should fall upon him, and that he
should die there.

The wicked also do desire to dye well. Nume. 23.
I pray God, that my soul may die the death of the ryghteous, and that my last
end may be like his, said Balaam.

Although Moses would not obey our Lords commandment, Deut^. 24
which would he should have passed over Jordan. Yet it seems that he would
gladly have lived longer, if it had pleased our Lord. For he says. Our LORD
is angry with me. Lo I must die in this land, and shall not go over Jordan.

A great part of the reward of Moses law, seemed to consist and stand in long
life. Deute. 32.
Set your haries unto all the words which I testifye unto you, for if ye
fulfill and do them, ye shall prolong your days in the land whether ye go, to
co^quere and to possess it.

became the instrumente of death, the which is, as it manyfestly appears
contrary to life, by the which we should come to life.

The which life the true author of eternal health, that is the way, the
truth, and life, and has the dominyon over death and life. Grant us. The
which with the father and the holy ghost, lives and raygneth one God world
without end. So be it.

FINIS.
